O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Here is the translation:
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in vision that I will complete this with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is strange to everything altogether, so the knowledge is perished and broken off, and nothing remains of it except for a few descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and are closed the intentions, and is alienated the knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I will bring it to life together with the ordering of this treatise according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of fire cauteries and other instruments of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation for it, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for that reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who intervenes to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of members, and their forms, and conjunctions, and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of vertebrae, and the arrangement and moving and resting muscles, and the origin of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And so Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and indeed in the art of handcraft.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should beware lest he make an error and kill people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	in such a way that I have seen many of those who interfere with this science and so abandon their knowledge and sense experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut out the abscess of scrofula or collarbone from a woman and cut the arteries of the collarbone.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	Why so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead between her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And a certain wise man who treated an arrow wound on an old man's leg, and the arrow was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died inside three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been summoned to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew that if it was not removed he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And a certain wise man who took care of the duke of our land who had his leg broken and with the breaking was wounded;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the wise men, full of ignorance, set the breaking on top of the wound in such a way that it was firmly fixed, and left no room for healing, and left him thus at the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commanded that he not be loosened at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and remained thus so that the leg became entirely gangrened and the toes came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come and untie the leg.
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I untied it so it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the way the corruption had already been confirmed in the member, and could not be healed;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another surgeon who burst an abscess that had become gangrenous, and then inflamed it by the wickedness of his authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a gangrenous sore, when it is purged of melancholic humor, does not agree that one touches it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And therefore, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	namely, one which has peril in several situations;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For which it is necessary that you keep them for yourself, so that the foolish mouth cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	Take your arms in order, and begin to treat your patients lightly and firmly, and follow the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and let go of the grievous illnesses of bad health;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and put away your doubts about what troubles you, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galien says in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Don't take on yourself a bad disease unless you're called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and medical cauterizations with water, and the chapters are ordered from head to feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the forms of instruments, and of fixings for cauterizations, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about poultices and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it is the chapters that are ordered and the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is the chapters ordered as far as the head, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, so that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of aid and detriment of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the quality of help, and of harm, is the longest word and subtlest science and secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and about these things many wise men spoke and agreed with them;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I am not satisfied with their words, because I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that fire-cautery helps universally to all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	it's to know warm complexion with regard to material, and dry complexion with regard to material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a warm and dry complexion together with material, some people divided and said that the fire cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that the fire cautery is not good for disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured for a hot disease by heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and those who said the opposite say that the fire cautery makes great help for hot and dry diseases that come in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you consider the body of man and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be so on some occasions through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in any case, do not intervene except by one who has experimented with it, and who knows by long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and the space of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	We have no fear of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is among the secrets of cures, and of greater good than burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth to another member unless it touches the one that is cauterized, and does no harm to any other member if it is not called upon.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medicines come from member to member by applying, and bring grievous disease to the afflicted member;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and it happens that the patient dies.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And I have found this by experiment and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and therefore I excuse the length of my speech, for it does not please me that I take away from you the secret which is revealed by fire and the quality of work, how it repels the diseases of bodies, as philosophers say in demonstrating;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive him in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and chose precedents.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harm that befalls is put right by the aid of the cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and likewise, if the cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for a later time when greater harm may come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think thus, dear son, as foolish men do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return.
et il le dient ensi;	and they say so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they think, because cauterization is not just a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries out the humors that are the cause of the pain, and excels in value for its hastiness and virtue of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And a possible thing is that the patient's illness comes at times according to their complexion, the place of the illness, and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and there are accumulated in him the excesses through the consumption of meats and similar things, unless cauterization is administered to the area where he has an abundance of excesses and moisture, as with hot cautery for pain, and similar things, and that same pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their intention is false, and it is said that cauterization is the last resort of medicine because when we administer treatments in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer the cautery, and it is good.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that cauteries of golden instrument are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and for its high substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the marks of a cautery do not produce disease, but this is not true for I have tested it and found that it is true in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauteries are more effective than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know how hot it is by the color of the gold, and it becomes cool at once.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	so they are burned to the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use fire cauterization that we have made apparent to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And I have arranged this chapter from the beginning up to here, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is worth for moisture and coldness on the head, and there are two ways in which it is done because of a disease that is called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, and to the ears, and due to multitude of dreams and pains of teeth and throat, and also for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, sode, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a soluble medicine, clarifying the third humour or the fourth, according to what virtues, age, and custom of the patient it can support.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient lie back.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed in your hands, and put his hands on your knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	and after that place the tip of your thumb on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and let come to you your two middle fingers, if it bleeds from then afterwards sharpen the cautery which is called "olivary", of which there is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make a downward and outward motion of your hand little by little in turning;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then lift up your hand slightly, and withdraw the instrument if you see the bone a little bit;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After take a little of silk, and put in soft and wet cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and let it be for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After placing a damp cloth on moist skin;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and leave it so until the scab is removed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the wound of anointing, which is called "tetrafarmaçon", as long as it remains sound.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the old men say that when a wound stays open longer, it purges more;
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore one should help it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should heat the cauterization until part of the bone is burned, and then stop what has been burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others say that one should make a fire cauterization as long as possible, and push it so hard that it reaches as far as the bone is wide, just like the women put in their flax combs so that the humors may flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After that, one should heal and bind.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to be good in every way, except for some men who have a way of fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should leave it alone;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by continuous natural fluxions, as we observe in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and even when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of a fire cauterization is more safe and gentle for me, and from this I work in such a way that I bring about salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain comes to the head and lasts long, then the patient should use year's resins and pills which are called "cochie", and for purging of the head, and with oils and emplasters.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one makes the cauterization that we have previously said, and it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care lest the patient's head be of strong constitution, and let it not be too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Then one must cauterize below this type of cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	Afterwards make a cautery on each horn of the head right up to the bone, just as we have said before, and make another one in the place which is called "vasselz";
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the place where one puts poultices;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and lift your hand so that you do not see right up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those used to cauterize the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	of the head's cauterization
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When sudden pain comes to one part of the head, and the disease extends as far as the eye, and the joint is purged by medicines of the world, and all the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases, and nothing helps;
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then he performs cauterizations by two methods, namely from medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauterization of medicine is that you take an almond, strip its skin and grind it into small pieces like two halves, and then make a temple on the spot where the pain holds in such a way that you can place the ground almond under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is placed, if it binds and strengthens well, and leaves it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind and treat the wound with garlic, and leave the sore thus for two or three days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put a poultice of buttered cotton on it until it purges itself.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment with ointment, as long as it remains sound;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that this is not good, then make use of some burning medicines that I have written or any other treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron cautery to which it pertains.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "clo" because the head is made in the shape of a clove or if there is a little curvature, and has a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and sets it on the painful place, and holds one's hand and turns the iron a little bit, until the middle of the spear that is to be burned.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and flow forth abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Then apply a poultice on top of it, and put it on the place for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply moistened cotton in butter, and then treat the place with ointment until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", do it all along the point, and take care not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of a headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously discussed in divisions of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the preceding cauterization about medicine and fire does not help, then you must heat the cauterizer which is called "cultellare" until it is white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and then place it on the aching spot a line of about half an inch long, and lift your hand once, and make sure you do not cut the artery and that it does not reach just to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the jawbone that goes limp when eating, and the nerves have regard only to the limpness and that spasms do not come to the patient, and beware of excessive bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or even greater fear for one who does not know how to deal with it, and is not experienced or studied;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the work to follow its way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how one stays bloodless when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauterizations do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the head also as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said or chapter of extracting the artery, with the cauterizer having two knives;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this cauterization is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear due to coldness, and one has tried medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not subside, then heat this cauterizing tool called "poins" to the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	Afterward, prick all around the ailing ear, or around both if the pain holds in both, and draw away slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the place to begin;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and have X points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure, let it be until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cauterization is not other than those that move with phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of disease;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not make a cauterization on similar things that come from scorbut and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this similar thing of torture that moves with phlegm from urine and purgations of head and gargling, and it does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one in the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cauterization in the part that appears healthy, and make it cauterize near the top of the ear on the edge of the head, and another one in the temple as long as a finger;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery go on until the middle of the key is burned away.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is like the appearance of a cutlery that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knives be a little bigger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the cure, let the wound be as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the head, and one at the place called "vessel" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	From lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	Give to the patient great years and pillowy substances for the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After that, apply to the head of the patient all, and place on the occuput a mustard plaster as written in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of the fire-cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it heals thus, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it does not heal, then make three fire-cauterizations inside the head from above down to the neck, and have a space of two days between each cauterization.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you see it swelling, and the patient is suffering, then make one cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if necessary, make two more on top of the two horns, and treat it until it is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	And let the cauterization which is called "olivare" be, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from chill of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleared of years and what we have said beforehand;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after that, the head of the patient is to be cauterized inside and on each horn, and then again behind and three times on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then do four cauterizations on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and leave it until the most bitter part is burned, and lift up your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the patient has been cured, and let the cauterization which is called "olivare" be, as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use a cautery except in the case of those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain with years and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffering from prolonged treatment.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a child who cannot otherwise suffer, then do gargarism and mastication to cleanse the brain often with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's leader is one hundred leagues away, and I make the cautery as we have said before, and I make the cautery on the vassal, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is far and suffering, I make the cauteries as I have said to one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, do one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and thick phlegm accumulates, then do those cauterizations of threads as we said for someone with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluities are declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, according to what is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After the king's leader of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after I make a linen wrapping well done, like a circle, and put it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and let the patient be crossed, and be well held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after present the lining, and make moves with old sheep's tallow butter;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and let the heat be tempered by fire, so that the back can bear it when poured on.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After clearing the circle from inside towards the head, and letting it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once a week with another good governance, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you wish to cauterize, make many points all over the iron.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cauterization moistens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on a wet cotton cloth in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the disease of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the disease comes first to the eyes by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink cleansing the head, and guard against all moistures, and make him sweat or take a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After this, command him to put his head back and make a cauterization on the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples if the descending flow of the humor is together in both eyes, or in one if the descending flow is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut off all the veins and arteries that are below the skull, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of bleeding of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop the flow with all your might.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you how to extract arteries and perform cautious incisions.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one makes a cauterization or cautery under the two bones that are behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are above the veins or near the arteries that appear at the top of the forehead.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is cold and humid excess, then make the cauterization I mentioned at the beginning of this procedure going down to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply a cauterization on the forehead, and two cauterizations above the two temples, and two cauterizations or cauteries under the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is necessary to do more, then apply a small cauterization on top of each little cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the body of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer the medicine according to what we said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three bitter hellebores to drink.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's beard, and make a fire cauterization on the spot of the olive-cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauterizations on the "clavilis" which is called above the two earlocks, a little below the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery so you don't cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And that is the form of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this iron called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	To which it pertains:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see, make two cauterizations on the two earlocks as long as the earlocks are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and don't remove your hand until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that points to the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyebrow is converted to a beard, and pricks the eye, and one makes cauterizations according to two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to know by fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cauterization, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they are equal and have grown, then put the patient in a good state;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	afterward mark on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and be the beginning of the sign below the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put damp cotton in egg white and powdered periwinkle on the eye, then heat the cauterize as is its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure you have marked point by point several times, so that the edges be burned away.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the sign of the health of the operation is that you see the paper contracted, and the hairs lifted to the level of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Lift your hand then, and let it be so for three days, then put a moistened cotton cloth in the poultice until the scab is removed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of ointment as long as they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after this the hairs come and the paper is softened then start the cauterizing again on that very spot just as you did first.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper is lifted to its natural place and is even, and does not prick the hair at all.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and live chalk, each one a third, and grind them together well.
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	et the way haste, so that it does not cool, then put on top of the form as you are made like the leaf of the myrtle tree, and place on top of paper eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the illness remains only in one oil alone, then it must be worked on that one, and also in both;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and place a moistened cotton cloth under the oil;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's joints are in your hand and place your thumb showing above the medicine, and press it gently every time the patient feels a stinging from the medicine, for he feels stinging also as if from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done all this, then remove the medicine from your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the stinging is gone, then lift the cloth away, and put it back as you see the paper lifted up just like if it had been lifted by constraint of fire or by cutting;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	But not so, then one should still apply more medicine to the wound or where the medicine has no effect, until all your works are equal and your eyes are in order.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a damp cotton poultice in butter as long as the burned area is covered, after curing the wound of ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you to beware well of your work with great caution lest there be no harm done to the patients.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hair pricks in the oil, then restart the medicine on that wound which is softened by the proper paper, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after it has been cured until it is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and that is the shape of the fern of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to how they are constricted;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and the right way is not shown to him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	I think I've reached the end of the text! The last line is simply "de la cure de fistule par cautere", which translates to "of the treatment of fistula by cauterization". This suggests that the treatise is moving on to discuss another medical topic, rather than continuing with the previous section.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the surgeon's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or change its position;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	then put damp cotton in egg white or in pear juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after that, warm the fire cauterizing instrument which is thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and shape it to fit the head like a feather from a vulture, along with the fire cauterizing instrument;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but still, this one that is shaped is good for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula is opened, and pulling out the pus, and drying.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and if it is closed, then work on it, and pull out the bowel;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after apply hot fire to it strongly, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the nose near the eye, so that your hands do not act foolishly;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and put the cautery in the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery just to the bone, then it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If not, then start the cautery again once more, or if you need to, and let it be for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after I put a moist cloth on butter and let the treatment of drying ointment continue until it is healed, and if forty days have passed and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and the king will follow according to what he will come into his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a method of fire cautery for a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	You understand a fistula, and close the opening;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after that, put in the slit a subtle camel's hair of which it is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and make it to the quantity of an inch of linen;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or camel's hair firmly, and do not let the patient move until the linen piece is applied to its place;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's wound a moistened cloth, either in the shape of eggs or in an awn;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the linen piece so closes the opening of the fistula, and the wound by marvelous sanitation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a poultice to the neck, and bring back the fistula to its proper place in the neck.

de l’aposteme de la goule	It looks like we've reached the end of the text! The last section is titled "de l'aposteme de la goule", which translates to "about the abscess of the throat". This suggests that the treatise is moving on to discuss another medical topic, rather than continuing with the previous section.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or in the uvula or the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after having made a purulent discharge and rot and has been envenomed and becomes a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in sections, but it does not benefit.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you make the fire cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the hole or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron comes to the bottom of it, and in its rear.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	due to movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and this does not help, then place the patient's head on your shoulder;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	after apply the fire cautery whose form will come hereafter in such a manner that you put a cord on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and put hot hastenings into the cautery and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	after lift up your hand and begin again the cautery according to your pleasure;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	after fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and let them keep it for an hour and rich fever.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gums made soft restrained, and the moisture corrupted dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When the toothache comes from cold or warmth, whether it is hot or cold, and medical remedies do not help, then there is need for a fire cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and butter cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Butter cauterization is such that you take butter from a cow, and shape it into an iron or earthenware spoon.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent needle, and soak it in melted butter, and apply it to the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And thus do this often until the virtues come to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the buttery wool and cotton are cold, then apply it to the aching tooth, and apply hot iron so that the fire comes to the tip of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cauterization together is such that you take an iron or earthenware cauldron, and it should be large enough so that the fire does not come to the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After the burning of the cautery, from which the form will come after this, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand so that the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fill their mouth with good butter in the application of this cautery, and then wash it away.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a cautery on whatever part of the head you want, and according to what you can.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the chain:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When scrofulas are of phlegm and cold moisture, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then burn the cautery with hair from which this form comes, and have two openings for the fumes to issue at the other part.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice as needed, until it comes to the edge of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and apply a wet cotton cloth wrapped in butter until the burning sensation is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after that, treat the joint with ointments and tents until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When the moors prevail on the pores of the person, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be cleansed first with soluble medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	then apply a cautery to the root of the throat, and take care not to come too close to the throat, and do not burn with fierce heat but only slightly.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After this, perform another cautery at the neck of the spine, and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" which we have described previously;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	of the throat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all and every illness of the pomegranate are caused by cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or heat, and it is an old disease, then make two cauterizations on the forehead in the veins.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery between the breasts.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, make a cautery in piercing all the cautery that is called "point" of which the form is described before in the illness of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the points be just up to thirty, or around that.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the limb according to what is said beforehand, and make the cauterization of three rinses according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of this are the cauterizers lighter, because you do three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then have the patient lie down on their back and on their side.
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the cure that is inside the little thing with your left hand on the patient's back.
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then apply the fire cauterization which has two needle prongs in this shape.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the cure until it pierces just to the side, and then come the figure of the cauterization together with four cauterizations.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and therefore it is made cauterization with the cauterizer that has three prongs, because the figure of cauterization is six cauterizations.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and that is the shape of the cauterizer with three prongs.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And at no time is added to this one nerve for which there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	After putting on the cautery, burn powder with silk.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	after making the patient rest and not moving the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little things happen then, and make a cauterization on the thick part of the cauterizing nail, or many cauterizations in piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is refastened, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come into the stomach, as long as they expel it to his complexion, and many cathartics are multiplied in him, and customary cure methods do not help him, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, stretch out his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	Then make three cauterizations below the navel of the belly to the quantity of an egg, with all the cautery clavicle, and two cauterizations outside on both sides until the shape of the cauterizations is at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they will not be joined together when they will give birth.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and be the cauterizations so deep that they reach the two parts of the kidney, and be the shape of the cauterizations according to this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a great cauterization in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and that person who has fear of this cauterization, cauterize in piercing and sign above the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you see in advance.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Then cauterize all the cautery which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When pain comes to the liver from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is greatly removed from its natural constitution by excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is treated according to what we have said in divisions, and it does not help him, then it is necessary that the patient be strengthened on his habit;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and mark three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria, where the ribs of a man come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and leave a space between each cautery the thickness of an egg;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauteries be long in the body, and do not press too hard with your hand on all the cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and burn only half of the key, and let the patient be upright on his feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then sit up, stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and that is the shape;
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you wish, then cauterize with the cattery, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the way through the skin, for you would cause the whole body to dry out;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and let it come just to boiling, for the skin is very subtle thereabouts, and you know well how it should be.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane;
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, then the patient feels pain that is not too strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if it is in the membrane, then he feels unbearable pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And then when this treatment was being done by the midwives, it is necessary that the patient be covered on his head.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign the spot where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a reed, because that is its shape.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery until the keys are burned, and come just to the spleen, until the purpuration is all cured.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure according to the treatment of sores until he is healed.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not necessary that anyone but he who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine should use this cautery, and through whose hands these diseases have sometimes been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly undertake it; and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cauterization for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancient ones say that one should make purulent cauteries with the roots of aristolochia, and in such a manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristology long, the largest you can find, and it should be dry, and also as big and as long as you need;
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and soak it in oil, and apply it to the fire, and cauterize with a cautery between the forceps and the neck, and two small cauterizations a little lower down in the part that is below the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining a little behind;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and one cauterization in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the ribs of the breast after the cauterization that is between the two shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press your hand, but rather hold it openly just as in smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And it is said by some ancient that someone should use fire cauterization to make the abscess resemble a razor, and heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess;
