Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down from the veins that are above the forehead of the head and it does not benefit at all from the medicine that is done, and you see the patient's face turning red, and feeling a numbness on the forehead as if in terror;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and when they are warm and moist so that the hairs of papyrus are fallen, and the papyrus is scalded and burned by the heat of tears, it has need of this remedy.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And the ancients called it "contused cure", and is that you do to the patient who has this disease, making three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and be one of the incisions also like two do inside the forehead going down to the nose and the others two by the sides above the papers and take care of not cutting into the arteries that are on both sides above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and move your hand away from the continuation of the two jawbones and be each wound the quantity of three fingers across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have prepared a piece of sponge and wet it with cloths to absorb the blood, then thrust the spatula in two parts as this is its shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is above the temple down to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape out all the kernel which is between the two incisions to the very surface of the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision down to the other second one, and then draw this spatula out.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	and insert into the first incision the instrument which is called "culterelle", and it is very well cutting on one side, and not cutting at all on the other side, and that's its shape.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And set the cuticle cutting towards the fatty part at the heart, and the cuticle soft towards the bone, and pull it so that it comes to the middle opening.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where the bone appears, and then do the same on the middle opening up to the other opening.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then draw out the blood evenly, and express the place for the taken blood;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put a cloth of old cotton in each opening, and place moist cloths soaked in wine, oil, and ale on top, and make sure that pustules do not form there;
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, release the bandage, and immediately administer a great amount of cold water, then apply the balm of basilicum with rose oil, and other remedies used for wounds, until he is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When someone comes with a great catarrh as usual, and you see the eyes tense and small, and weakening sight, and burned paper;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and in the forehead there is intense pain, and the patient groans;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know through these accidents that those materials and the cautery do not come forth from many voices, and the mother takes care of what is there, so it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great gash in the forehead, and another of moderate width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin at the left side of the forehead to the right, and let the incision be just up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and remove your hand from the temples that move when eating;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, then wipe out all the blood with a sponge, and then cover between the two lips of the wound and put old linen cloth, and try linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then lay damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, and beware of hot abscesses;
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is opened, then you should rub the bone until flesh begins to form, then treat with things that bring forth flesh.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of barley flower, and four parts of safflower, and make an ointment.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds so that the flesh may heal throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	Everything that drips from the ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or stones, or iron splinter, or similar thing like iron;
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seed, such as jasmine, vetches, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things like water and vinegar and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it settles in the ear or another way that does not belong to the ear and does not grow there, nor grows in the ear, then put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if it yields any drop of purple oil or sesame oil, then apply an extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make it sweat with condiments, and stop the nostrils when the sweating comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and it extends above the ear.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times harm comes from this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, then administer extraction with fine tweezers, of which there is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it jumps forth at the tweezers, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then administer extraction with a fine thread of small doubling;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not jump at that, then make a leaden chain and insert the end of the chain or ear plug into the hole in the ear very strongly, and stop what is around the chain with soft wax so that blood cannot enter with the chain;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	then pull it forth firmly, for many times harm comes as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come forth in this manner, then take fat of which takes the birds, and put in some instrument that is sharp to do so, and wrap a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue on the stone or whatever it is, and draw forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she does not jump away from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear before the abscess appears and spasms.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of cutting is that you first let the patient's cephalic vein bleed and extract the blood according to its power, then sit the patient between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear at the fatty part or dependent part.
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and make the incision like a moon, as long as you come to the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and care for it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it's pus that forms and swells, then administer an extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if he cannot get out, administer a spatula-like instrument held subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and bring an incision of that kind.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist from the ear moisture, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then strain it through subtle pincers and a press, just as we said, so that the extractions are light.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water then that runs into the ear, it is fitting for the patient to use an external poultice first, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it be bound on that very ear itself where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps away because of this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, take many pieces according to the length of your should be held tight and light, and heat them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient's ear orifice in your own hand, and lift up from below with his fingers on the other side, and strike with another instrument on top of the bone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop striking one piece against another until all the water flows out, and thus it jumps all out;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, then take the stick, and put one end in the ear, and the other end is pressed with fire until the stick is well burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then redo the other side of the sticks as long as all the water has dripped out, just as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small, such as a rabbit and similar things, treat it just as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is large enough to be felt, then make an incision with forceps.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and that is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of moles from the ears, when you have treated it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you look at the ear to the sun:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there is no opening anywhere, then treat them with delicate tweezers, and if not, take the cord that has the form here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle thread into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then pull strongly on the cord.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then wrap around the cord with cotton as I said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	And if they do not emerge as we said, then administer distillations as the ancient ones have proved in the killing of worms, and you will find or treat about distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, according to the form that is here, as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether it is of silver or of lead, large below at the small holes, and above for distilling.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press inside the distillation by the lead instrument well-made for this, and if you see take the file and envelop it around the point advantageously with cotton.
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then pour in your oil or juice, and as much of your medicine as you see fit in the cane, and the cane be in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then insert into the file all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be heated by fire so that it can be distilled in the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without any hole in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through the bursting of a wound or the growth of a tumor within the ear, and these burstings sometimes go very deep into the ear so that it cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes the hole bursts forth again, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which goes very deep and cannot be seen is a serious wound in many dispositions, and what can be seen requires that you place the ear of the patient in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opacity appearing, then the work is all in this space where it takes its shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be gently and carefully placed before and behind all smooth, so that it does not hurt the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	The skin of the opening is of bone or flesh of the ear, so hold it with subtle pinchers and cut it lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the obstructions are deep in the ear, then take a subtle razor and heat it slightly with fire, then put it into the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you sense the opening that makes the patient feel sorrow to hear, pierce lightly, and beware that you do not wound the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian myrrh.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this every day until the wound is closed, or take a tent and moisten it with pink water, and powder it with vitriol bronze.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary that you remove the tent and put another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then care for him until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the discharges of blood come forth, then dip a sponge and wring it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the discharge of blood which are found in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of paperwax
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This other thing that comes from the eyes when they are moist and dry, so you must stretch it with forceps and pincers, and cut off a spatula's width of its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then place it on a leaden plate.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if it does not crack, then cauterize with the lenticular fire caustic, and the cauterizer after the incision is worth nothing.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times repair, so that nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	Of the Hellebore
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come from the eyes things that seem like hoarfrost in their shape and hardness, and because of this is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take heed that the rain falls from one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make the incision wide, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with tweezers and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cut it without piercing a little bit of parchment, it will cause no harm to the patient;
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if the wound is large, then sew it together with a suture, and care for it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, then do not apply pressure, because the swelling will restore itself soon and will form flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the rain is running down inside the ear towards the top, then reverse the parchment, and take with tweezers, cut and press from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it hurts nothing;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the poultice is applied, then wash the eye with salt water and care for the place where the wound will form until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fat that is applied to the papers above, and this happens more in children than in no one, and it hurts very much to their eyes, and they come with catharrs in the mornings, and are unable to gaze at the sunlight because the tears rush to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because of this they lie down on their faces quickly, and sleep above, and have their papers below their eyelids dampened by the swelling and appearance that has covered the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the lid to your eyes and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on a stone;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains each part, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two hands from one side and the other, so that the parts be assembled within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula's edge, cutting a notch of moderate width, and it should not be any larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin smooth until you come to the part that contains;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in various positions comes forth from the notch, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Then extract it thus as one piece of cloth wrapped between your hands at the back, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and beware that you do not insert into the incision, so you do not come up to all the spatula just to the eye, so you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the exit wound does not open in the beginning of the incision, then slightly enlarge the incision a little so it appears.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then pull it out as we have said, then moisten the cloths with ale and water, and put them on the wound, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who burn it and put it on top in order to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the aposteme comes hot to the skin, then apply emplasters soothing it until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When paper hairs grow that are not natural, and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, and bring on mannerisms of diseases such as tears accustomed and softening of the papers and white spots, until it is a cause of the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and there is the cure according to four manners:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by fire cautery together, or by medication according to what is before this chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by canines, according as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary to put the patient's head on your shoulder, then turn the paper of oil to your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If she is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then put an needle on all the thread above.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be on the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow at those hairs, and draw the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make in the part below the paper, below the adjacent hairs, all along the scapular region, from the great wound to the small one.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull out the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then draw on the paper an image of a hedgehog, like the shape of myrtle, and yet it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see to unfold the paper which is divided in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if someone has need, they should take a great quantity of paper according to what the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then make a small spatula on both sides of the two lines that you have marked, and begin to smooth out the great lump just a little.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And be one of the slits near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the thread in one of the two corners of the leather, then scrape all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then assemble the two lips with a stitch of an needle and all the thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make sure to remove any excess threads on both sides of the stitches for any sticky things, if you see that.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, don't bother with it, then leave the stitch and threads for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound without sewing or constraining things, for the paper comes to life at the suturing of the wound and its assembly, but sewing is deadly (as the ancients said), and it is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you sew the paper in a shape which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, in three separate sections, according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut off what rises above the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps and the things are not equal, take a needle with one thread and push it into the shape.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and push the other thread through the large border, and the second thread through the small one, and tie them together between your two threads equally.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above which you have sewn, as we have counted, then tie the two lips of the wound with sewing, and care for it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to the incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar calming ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and sometimes it happens that the hair of the parchment is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	so you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of the sinews is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you should transform the parchment and the hole within according to what I have said, then make two sinews by art, and two subtle ligaments as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and tie the two knots of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly on what rises from the parchment of oil, and strain the two sinews of the two parts together;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it remain thus for some days, and the skin that was stretched will die and wither and harden, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is delayed, if it is bound by some strength, then let the wound be treated until it is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is closed, and if the skin has been lifted up, and they can no longer be pricked by hairs.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and this is the shape of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the works are such that you take a fine needle, and put in it a thread of soft and subtle silk.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then tie the knots together and tie one to another subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm in length.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order another fine thread of silk briefly, and knot the ends of the thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head on your shoulder;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be done in the sun so that the work is declared, for this is a subtle and small work; then insert the needle into the root of the hair joined together, and make it pierce the paper quickly as you move it above the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then pull out the hair up to the needle, and insert into the needle that hair, if there is one, two, three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then pull out your hand until the hairs come forth all along the needle in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the needle is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, then pull out the needle from below all the thread that you have arranged, until the needle comes forth from the orifice above and you see it by the sight of the eye.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then if you draw the bowstring and thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hairs grow back in their place and the skin heals above.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany them with long hair from the nearest goat's natural growth, and be joined with it or leave it, until they grow out and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the dimness of the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the purtification comes into the eye, there are two ways.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural and one unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or incision, or cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of treatment is that you cut open this swelling, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen cloths, and tie it until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not necessary that you use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	If you do this, then the illness will return worse than the first one.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but the work of soft things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose of water or high and flaxseed be cooked, and the anointing with dissolved aquilion in some oil, and wrapped in a tent, and the treatment for these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your treatment is that you give yourself guard so it does not harden at all according to its former form;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are far from the remedies for this disease, so it does not return according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh that comes to the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness that truly is called "axacrati" below which is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds and gashes and cauterizations and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the method of treatment is that you take a needle with a doubled thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left armpit to the right, so that the thread comes out through two joints of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then is the flesh above to all the needle, and the cut to the spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should be, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take the razor and put it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits or one on each side within the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and be the edges of the two slits at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as if it were the letter "I Greek";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then take that flesh, according to the quantity of its edges being worn away below, from what precedes the paper, then add the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of wool;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then perform the treatment for what we have said regarding softening medicines and tents until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a break or a cut or a cauterization, then you must make a clean incision below the hairs of the papyrus, and according to what is written before.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then sever between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare an instrument for every possible skill as to how they make the figure return to its natural shape.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is required of work and instruments in various conditions.
dou soudement de la papiere	from the sudden movement of the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this stitching occurs in the same way as the paper above is sewn with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural activities, then it is necessary that you put the tip of a razor under the paper and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and the stretching should be done by pinching, until you obtain what is subtle in the spatula-like, which is neither too aggressive nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot bear if the spatula is too aggressive and damages the eye.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, which you make on the assembled part, should be done lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and all that is assembled should be healed, and make no impression on the salty water of the eye, nor raise up sweet water and gall.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put a cloth of linen between the paper and the eye, and place moist wool on the eye in abundance of egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days' use of gall and similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the ulcers of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the finger is in two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	She is nervous and similar to a hard boil, and another one that is not at all nervous, but is similar to frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and heated in pincers cannot be overcome.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both kinds of appearance begin towards the great tear duct, and grow little by little until it covers all the sight and all the light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts their head on your shoulder, then you open the eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lifts up the paper to your hand, then cools it with pincers of small doubling, and stretches it above.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert a hair from a horse, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the swelling, and push all the way through with the whole needle, and tie the swelling with a thread and stretch it above, and scrape off the rest on the side of the swelling that faces the tear duct and the silk to the hair just up to the head, then cut the remaining part at the root of the tear duct by all the fine and subtle forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear duct as usual, so that through the incision the body will not produce tears habitually.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and sometimes the finger nails grow to the cuticle alone, and onto the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then one scrapes off all the softened scab from which this shape comes:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be sure that the scab does not touch the fleshy part and break it, and that the blister is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour a little bit of safflower oil into the wound, and make a poultice with litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat him according to what is needed until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the finger is not numb, and you cannot push the needle in, and the cuticles cannot enter, this kind of fingernail condition is often cured by medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow as I have told in the section, and if you see it cover, then anoint the patient's oil and take a light scab with a gentle poultice according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And gently pull the eye upward; and if you see that it does not lessen and the reason is hastened to it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red copper oxide, and stop the eye just until the next day.
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, as it is inflamed with apostema, then apply a poultice and cure the hot abscess until it is healed; then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hurts the eye greatly, then suspend it with an ointment, and cut off a part but not all, so that the tears may not come forth.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then distill into the eye a red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the conjunctiva
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men do not always have red flesh, and it covers the pupil and holds steady above the papillae and turns away from the forehead, and seems like a rose of mulberry.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work is such that the patient places their head in your hand, then works the eyes, and binds all that flesh with suitable cords to it, and holds it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then cut the first layer of skin, and go on cutting all the way to the razor's edge, and take care that you don't injure the eye in the work;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be like the spatula that we have said in the incision of the ulcer and with small forces one can remove the scab, as the form shows after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, then apply oil of sainfoin broth or where you distill red vinegar and similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and put on top of the eye a cloth with egg white, so that it may be assured of an aposteme hot;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if it remains unattended, and the blood surges up, and you doubt an abscess is hot, then leave off the eye and treat the hot abscess with soothing things for a hot abscess.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make the sore join together in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But nonetheless, you should hasten the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and by the accidental way, in iron work;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand on any of these works until you see that those members are suffering from this treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red when they are covered on the eye, and tolerate the work of their sight and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is therefore necessary for you to first look at the eye, in which the swelling is, is big, and there is no other disease besides the swelling.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then cool it in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your care, then stop those veins at all costs according to his wisdom, and let the veins be subtle and double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two eyebrows by degree in one flesh according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then compress those veins subtly and stop the blood an hour after another, until you see those veins move away from the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not stain the eye with the points of spittle, and do this work at the hour of noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you do not spoil those veins;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains in the sable.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you are unable to compress everything in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it be for some days until the pains are eased and you are assured of the abscess being hot, then resume according to this manner which is before, until he is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and that's the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the pus of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The physician is called "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there must be a reason in him that you cut on the abscess, there where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then remove all the instrument that is there in its form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "asperge chief", and be made of fine iron indented in the same chief again, and pointed like a file as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And put it on the surface of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and make so that at any time, then restore the place of medicines exactives.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the wound is bound, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bowstring is bound, and remains so for forty days, and it does not heal and is not apostemed, and no evil accident comes to it, know that it is sound.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	if not, then there is no other remedy but to bring back the fistula to the bottom of the nostril according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and it is that you uncover the bone the second time by iron and by old medicines, and when it is uncovered take the force according to this form, and let the point of the iron be at three angles, and let the fistula be thinned out to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then place it on the bone near the edge of the forehead, and remove your hand from the eye socket, then turn back to the force until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it because the vein goes in if they hold their hand on their nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and then restore the place of dry medicines as I have instructed you, and when the flesh has grown and hardened the places, so the matter goes into the night.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are fully open and there is no hindrance or decrease in the night, it is necessary that you hold the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the wound, then put poultices or hot cloths to suck, then apply on top of the eye a mixture made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarsaparilla, and then strain the eye and plaster it with bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and fold each one into four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eyes have need of.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	Then strain above with a strong bandage firmly, and reapply the poultices to suck without hurting.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	Then remove the poultices and leave the oil constricted day and night, and if the swelling increases, so it is necessary to bind tightly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	Then remove the binding after a day and a night, and if you see the oil repairing itself, it is good.
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	so reapply the plaster and cloths and the binding and poultices until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the bursting of the eye's skin
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come to the open vein, then opening, and comes forth like little pieces of resin, and it is appalling to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Then if you see it closing, the operations are such that you thrust a needle into the root of the part below up to where it is above, then thrust another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the wound.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then tie the thread of the double thread around the joint and bind a part of the vein around it, and tighten it well, then pull out the needle and put on the oil-soaked linen cloth in abundance of egg white.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it so that the thread takes hold with the vein, then care for the oil with soothing things until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and at no time is the wound restricted by the vein each part of a cloth circle until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if the eyes give a great appearance, then make an incision at the subtle spatula that comes from inside the oil, and drain the moisture with albugine and lower the eyelids, and enter it soon.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then pull out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is not except in the eye which is gathered together, resembling a water descending, and it is not water.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	and the manner of appearing of the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight chair, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it so that you see the boil come up above to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then let it be fixed, and not descend, and allow the light to fall on it, and see the patient's things as he used to.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the boil's descent is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	then make the patient sit in your hands, then take the subtle spatula and insert it on the keratinized skin up to a little above the conjunctiva with the keratinized membrane and crown, until the boil issues.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is released, so it drips in hot clear water mixed with honey or with vinegar and honey, then it should be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have the likenesses of waters in our division, and what is necessary for piercing;
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if one works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind the good eye very tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	then take in your right hand if the eyes are left, or in your left hand if the eyes are right, the instrument called "almagda".
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a finger in that spot above the eye to the part of the lesser tear; then insert the instrument called "almagda" virtuously, and turn your hand so it pierces into the blenchor of the oil, and sense that almagda comes to the empty thing.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is fitting that the measure of the way Almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the purl to the end of the nourishment.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	and this is the crown of the oil;
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the parchment crown, and then place the instrument just above where the water is, then press downwards on one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	The patient sees water flowing now, so the patient sees it before him and the instrument is in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting for a little while, and if the water rises back up the second path, place the force with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not go up, then extract Almagda gently by turning your hand little by little.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then place in water a small amount of gemstone jelly, and leave the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put aside the oil that is soaked in wool or linen moistened with rose oil and a quantity of egg white, and tie it with pure oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our time, apply cooked broth with a lot of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men whose eyes are too hard, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and not go too far inwards, but make a subtle hole, then put in alumada, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient and doctor to come, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark room.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and be still from all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and be bound according to his condition for three days.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then unbind him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day;
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is not necessary to do this in the time of the treatment or after the incision now, but rather you should wait, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	If an abscess appears, instruct that one to open their eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards what soothes the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is appeased, then open the eye and put a poultice on their face to cover any day, and be there in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	And then go out of the dark house step by step, and turn back into one's usual state;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And one came to us from the land of Yemen who told us that in their country they used to make a certain type of bandage that would help with swelling, but I have never seen any such thing in our land nor do I ever read about it in ancient books.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are likenesses of the forms of epilepsy, because he who does not know them sees.
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are properly of stone;
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of the same subtlety, and their ends in three angled aqueducts.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the nail
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	No times are born or arise without diverse lumps attached, because there are some that seem like scorpions at many points;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if it has such or is encrusted with flesh of a fiery color, and if the lump is soft of a white color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that then of these lumps which is soft and not encrusted, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and work his nostrils, and pour the wine onto those lumps, and treat them with fires;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then apply what you can sustain to the spatula of fine cutting on one side, as long as you know that lump is entirely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any part that cannot be covered, then cut it off with all the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if it does not bother you, or abscess forms, then cleanse it as it is fitting;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it as much as the blood is poured out and all the pus is removed, then pour on some water or cold wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the poultice does not work, and moisture comes just to the palace, know that it is healed;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is bone newly formed above the bone, to which instruments do not come to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then it is necessary that you put a piece of linen thread about an inch thick in it, and have it well greased by hand, and have between each night's space a little interval or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the patient's head into the cloth of the nettle in their own power, and pull it out in an aromatic way until it comes down through the nose into the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and many times do this with children at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and pull them out one after another just as we do on the cloth;
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this as long as you know that the night has corrupted that flesh, then pull out the thread, stop the bleeding, and moisten the thread with Egyptian oil, and put it back into the nose just as before;
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	do this for three days or more, until the salve corrodes all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	and then put on a new bandage made of linen some days until it is healed, and if he needs drying medicines, so use them;
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, through which one distills the oils and medicines or bandages:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it is of silver or of iron, resembling an open lamp like a candle, and guides also;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, make a bandage closed, and the instruments full to purge the head;
