et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and have some cloth at the head to hold it in place when one heats the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from the nail
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there occurs on the head a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes great over time, until it becomes something to behold by looking at it;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is necessary that you cut off the affected part at the beginning, and remove all the decayed matter, then put on the cauter or burning medicine;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you wait to cover it until it is large, then be aware if it is hard, with a faint color, poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	so do not touch it at all with iron because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it even once, great harm comes to the patient;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is of soft touch, not with faint color, and you see that it can be fully cut away, then empty the patient and cut it away without fear, and treat the joint in things constricting and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nail is cut off and cleansed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knows that when solutions of continuation come in one of these joint workings, it profits little, rather than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, one must then see what happens to each, so look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then place the two lips together with a suture, and then treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then it is necessary that you scrape away all the parts of their crust until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and bind it, and powder on top of powder with dragon's blood, and burn incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put on the powder a piece of plastery ointment or another ointment sticking together, and leave it until it cures by itself, then anoint with oil until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The way of the stitching is that you assemble the parts:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	of the apostemes of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In many cases there are within the lips abscesses that are hard and resemble grains of mustard, smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and incise on each side, and take up with tweezers and cut in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply oil to the wound after the vitriol incision, until the blood is stanched.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then ease the joint, and treat the bone with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times a whitish substance appears on the gums which the old people call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	so it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the flow of pus or blood continue.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put on the bone vinegar broth, or other drying and restraining powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that flesh returns after the incision, and it happens many times, then cut it again, and cauterize it;
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are foul and rough.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes teeth are black and yellow and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth smell.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	so you should make the patient sit in your hands, and his joints be in thy faith, and receive the teeth or scabs as they appear, until there is nothing left.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make a powder of blackness and greenness, and of yellowness and the other taints, until they are purged.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if you remove what is at the first reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	unless this, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that the teeth have need of diverse forms of instruments to remove, according as the work shows, because the scraper which one uses to remove teeth has other forms than he who uses it between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others shall be equipped with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you delay pulling it as long as you can, for this should not be done hastily.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance just up to that point where one has no excuse for regret.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain about the pulling tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain would drive the patient mad, and think it was from a tooth of Saint, and make someone pull out the good tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and yet the pain does not depart from him because of this, until the bad one is removed, for we have already seen that it happens to these saints.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you cut around the tooth to the whole gumline strongly in order to keep the gums from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move it to your fingers or with subtle forceps at the first pace and pace, until it is well separated, then firmly secure the forceps;
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the patient's joint be in your holy place between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump forth, then take one of these instruments and insert it lightly into each part, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the tooth is pierced and wounded, you should fill it with cloths, where the holes are;
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you strain it subtly with forceps, so that it does not break while being strained;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to cover carefully around the gum for dislodging the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And it does well to guard that you do not break it, and one part remains, and returns to the patient through the wickedness of the root with greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And take heed that you do not act like the foolish healers who, through their haste and boldness, sometimes break the carriage and do not bring what we have told;
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but often bring great harm by the extraction of roots that remain or by breaking the carriage, as we have often seen;
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is loose, wash the place with vinegar or asparagus and seaweed;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply the place with vitriol powder;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if that doesn't work, burn it with a cautery.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of extractors, by which one removes the teeth first, should be long and pointed with thick handles, so that they do not break when you pull out the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick handles so they do not bend when pulled, and be well made of iron, and have teeth to hold in place.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the roots remain in the socket, it is necessary that you put a moistened cloth soaked in butter on the place for one or two days, until the socket becomes softened, and then insert the forceps called "algefri", by which the head seems like a bee's stinger;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and be made inside like a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a scraper, by which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be big and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out for this reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, then help yourself with all the instruments, from which forms come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument having two handles, by which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in proportion to the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles great forceps, by which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be such that they cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and wise and subtle masters find by themselves the instrument that suits them best, according to what their works and the disease demonstrate, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to the diversity of cases; and if it does not break on the cartilage or other bones, or wherever it can, one should seek out the instruments that are needed, as I have said, and be aided by gestures, from which comes the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be thick and well-held to hold the bone, lest it escapes, but be able to hold and remove.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if it has putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, so treat it with all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the teeth appear not in accordance with the natural shape of the body, and their form is ugly, and especially in young women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly grown after the previous one, and is not in its rightful place, and cannot be straightened or filed:
adonques lou raie;	then draw;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is rough with the tooth, then take this instrument whose shape is shown here, and resembles a small beak, and be of iron with a sharp point in the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file files and files a little by day because of the hardness of the tooth, and for that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, then file with a similar file which has this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like a file used to make needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in lime the tooth becomes less and less heavy day by day, so it does not move until it falls out;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the tongue becomes smooth at the end with no roughness, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it is necessary to file down the roughness so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth is knocked out or falls out through percussion or falling, and the patient cannot eat what they want without choking, and you have treated them with constricting medications, and this does not help;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	so they must be restrained by a thread of gold, for the threads of silver become green and putrid, but the gold ones never change;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the middle thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	et if you wish to straighten the teeth, then take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the head [of the thread] between my teeth, if there is one or more of them, until you come to bleeding just up to a healthy tooth on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then begin the covering just to the part where you started, and strain your hand subtly and bleeding, until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your cord be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then bend the ends of the thread into pincers, and join them together, and reattach between the healthy tooth and the toothless one, so that it does not wound the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it thus tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes undone or the thread breaks, then bind it with another string.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it remained and served thus all its time, and that is the form of the teeth and the shape of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, bit by bit, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and doesn't meddle with it unless one is wise and skilled, and sometimes makes the form of a whalebone tooth, and puts it in the place where there is a deficiency, and holds it so as we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of removing the ligament from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	At no time does this happen that comes from under the tongue or natural origins, unless one is born so;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by an accidental wound that has been stitched up;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you will operate on the patient's mouth, and have their head in your healthy hand, and lift up the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then tie the ligament nervously to the wide one, so that the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, it is a sudden wound, then bind the bandage and tie the ligament.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and make sure that the incision is not too deep in front, for the artery which is below;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done that, lift the lever of rose and easy water, or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and keep the patient's tongue wrapped each night, so that the wound cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if hemorrhage comes forth, then put a vitriol plaster on top of the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the blood swells, then cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery which is good for that;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the doctor of another doctoring until he is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a boil that's yellow or black or hard, and the patient doesn't feel it, don't touch it at all, for it's a carbuncle;
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it's declining into gangrene, and there is moisture, then one must lance it, and the pus will flow out in a subtle spatula-like manner, and deliver it from both sides;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the blood flows against your work, then put on a vinegar poultice until it is stopped, then return to your work as long as you are treating all parts;
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from ease and from strain, and treat other treatments until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Sometimes a boil comes inside the throat called "godath", and they are properly called two almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If this is a postulate of small sense and of fusel color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the roots are large, then do not touch it with iron, also for the dismemberment of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but leave it until it is dead, and then you will take it apart, or it will break apart by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and the roots are subtle, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first make sure that the postulate settles down and is pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his hands be in thy right hand, and open the mouth and take hold of the tongue between thine own hands, and press the tongue under all the instrument, thereby is the form.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it shall be of silver or of subtle lead, just like our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and pierce it into the almond, and pull it away above as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not take anything from the cloths with it, then cut off at the instrument, so that is its form, which seems like one of great force;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and yet the head is curved, and one way against another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or of steel;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cut with pincers, which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	and be cut on one side and not on the other;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, and hot and easy, and if bleeding occurs, then gargle the patient with water or cooked pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped;
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment until he is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat except for the two almonds, so cut them then as the two almonds are equal.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, namely the abscess of little sense;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and I had nearly closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she stayed like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two pustules through the two holes of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I then hastened and made an incision in one place, then the abscess burst open, and drew out a great portion of pus.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I made another incision on the other side of the abscess, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After applying the poultice to these abscesses, and taking out a part of it, and no more came forth except for a small amount of blood;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the passage of the throat in the woman was stopped, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut at this abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscess recrossed again, and filled the place that I had emptied, so that it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I bandaged it and cautery was done inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	and thus it stopped growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and only God did anything with them after me.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the swelling comes down to the eye, and it is swollen and long, then it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if she is under a large and rounded one, so it is called "uvē".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When she is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess is appeased, and she is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut her out.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is rounded and assembled and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and she is sanguinary or of a red or black color, then it is necessary that you avoid making an incision on her.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, then, when you see her, according to the manner that I have said, of her length and thickness, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue onto the instrument which we have made a record of previously.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the pessary into the uvē, and train it downwards, and cut with both instruments which I have said in the incision of two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you not cover at all more than the excessiveness that is beyond the natural boundary.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you cover more, you cause harm to voice and word.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being covered, you should use artifice at the cauterization to calm their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and thin.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts their head in your hand, and then presses the tongue onto the instrument which we said in the chapter of cauterization, and confess with live water cold, so that it is not too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and use the point of this instrument, as to which there is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have on your head a beard or place where you put the medicine, just like the hairs of a comb, and put the instrument all over the medicine on the ulcer.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be seated on his couch, so that the saliva and spittle run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and the wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the ulcer, for the quantity of half an hour, until you see it congealed and the pustules of the medicine are appeased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take a piece of cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the entire cotton in the sheath above, until the cotton adheres to the ulcer.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and repeat after 3 or 5 days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to start again the cauterization of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cauterization, clean around the ulcer with cotton soaked in butter, and purify everything that is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be treated with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, not the fire cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured through fumigation in this manner, take calaminth and ysoop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put a little bit in it, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot be well glazed with hard earth, and inside the pot have the instrument shaved according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And be of silver or lead, and let one of the keys be inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is deadened;
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	afterwards it often begins again, until the eye dries, and be sure that you do not do this at the beginning of the swelling of the abscess, for many things happen there;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make them do anything except at the decline of an abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if these instruments are not present, take a cord and put a candle made of egg-white inside the head, so that the patient's mouth does not have too much heat.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the candle made of egg-white does not let the vapour weigh on the mouth, and it is a good treatment together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times one uses at the throat or spine of a fish, or something else;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you try what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing move.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what does not open for you and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit at once when the meat is cooked in the stomach;
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if the harsh things come out through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a root of lettuce, or a dry bread crumb;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and then thread is tied to the sponge, and then it is swallowed again;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes to the stomach, if it stays, then you will pull out a lot;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, then take the instrument of forceps according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And be the instruments curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high upwards;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest all life come forth, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and be careful that the patient pushes the instrument, because it is better for the thing to come out forced;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	If the bag is below, or he pulls it far away from all the instruments evenly, until it is far.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the discharge from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	There is no bloodletting in medicine, as I said in the division, by the treatment of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not benefit at all, then look in the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press his tongue onto the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sweat, so treat it with a small bandage or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, then take a knotted cord, and put it around the patient's throat, then tie the knot in the cord hot with fire, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is afflicted by water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full view of cold water, and open the mouth, and spit it out without swallowing, and move it with his hand often;
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if blood soon feels the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not stop as we said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the ear;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	It happens many times, for she will fall without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where it has coal ashes, and the cover is covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and in that hole is the key of the instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	Then you pour out the fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes just to the sweat.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and now the sweat falls, and if it doesn't fall, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, and takes bitter and salty things, and does not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it becomes necessary for him to go away by means of this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one draws out the pus is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved forceps for entering the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and has a resemblance to a doctor's beak, and it has a roughness like limestone, such that what it takes, it cannot let go;
et vez ci la forme:	and thus is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many kinds of abscess are, according to what is remembered hereafter on both sides in this book, and they differ in perforation and size;
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and it is in two ways, one being its own resemblance, and because of the moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are at the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of the fatty tissue are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if an abscess is not to be pierced, until the bow has been measured according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are dry, and do not die according to their completion, as abscesses which are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints, and one leaves them until they are rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is why it is a cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the abscess is below the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is mortified, it will harm the main limb.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	where it is below the foundation, if one pierces it even when it is dead;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess that is unripe and undigested, except for the one below the foundation, lest it will not penetrate far enough and be prolonged inside, and a fistula will ensue.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in due time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary that you know the time of perforating the abscess which is dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and healing of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you place the puncture or more dependent upon the abscess, and where it opens up movements;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the puncture should be long in the body, and if the abscess is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pain.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	Those who are bent, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in its natural place, you should leave the opening so that it is confirmed by complete digestion as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce before this, the body will be lengthened with blood from it, and filled with much waste matter.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance harden the lips and the deep parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is any abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you bring forth small abscesses, small ulcers;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great abscesses, great ulcers, and many splits according to the resemblance of the greatness of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to search out the cause, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become like a piece of cloth that is worn out and is dead, so one should do the same thing with babies:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if it has such ones that are split into three angles, and if there are such ones which one cuts away like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses from the kidneys;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if it has such ones where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar coping.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, like a soft and superficial abscess, it is necessary that you let them drain freely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you let it drain, if you do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but rather one part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess just until the next day, then do not touch anything above it;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do right by many times bit by bit, until the bowel empties completely.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	likewise if the patient has little strength, or women bearing, or small children, or old men who are worn out.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits leap away at times with the exit of the bow; so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not take heed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Then therefore proceed with great caution through this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound is small, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it's a clean cut, then try to apply some linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it's a large abscess and there are many perforations, then you must pack each one with a tent so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin and you have wrapped it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a clean cloth without moisture, and bind it just until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the surgeon, and the doctor of ointment, until he is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleedings occur in your work, so provide cold water and easy, and damp cloths, and set it on the bleeding place by many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the flowing of blood persists, then administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said to put in hands in this book, and if it is in the season of spring, and the flesh or abscess is very nervous, then you must put on tents and wet cloths soaked in wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer, and the flesh is fatty, then you must put on wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then release the abscess and the pus and the wound, as it is necessary, until he is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	I have told you how one must proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of blisters
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or when the hair of the head comes forth small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in wefts, as a tailor of a silk, and there is much of the same.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fat and such that also have moisture like pimples;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are others that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt that the artery will not go against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you try out every instrument called an "entromissoire", from which its form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then heat it above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, scrape away without leaving anything of the skin that contained that moisture, for it returns again if you leave anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then plunge in Egyptian oil if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, then in water and vinegar, and apply the dressing to the wound, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and those who remain will run with night dew.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then reapply the cotton as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of night dew.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of oiling as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds little fat, cut it according to this shape, from long.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and scrape out the ulcers, and flay off all around, and put all your care of drawing forward from where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the artery does harm to you, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is pustular, and to cut and to cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the pustular abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, for they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and one of the abscesses that I cut open was on the head of an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess just like a dry, rough, and white stone, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had cut into it, they would have made as much of a wound as in a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming from the head, except those that come to the heads of children and the roots of ears, the opening should always be at its most dependent place, in order for the pus to issue forth.
et les cure si com il covient.	and it is cured as is fitting.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck and below the armpits, and in some groin areas; sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are very large, and some are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each scrofula is properly inside its own coat, like the boil and abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and similar things to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one then which you see of good disposition to be touched, and is like in color to the flesh, and quiet on each side and is not harsh against the nerves of the neck or the artery or the canal, and is not too deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	so it is necessary that you cut above, and flay each part, and there are two lips of the key on the nodes, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	et the wound is small and small, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let it not be the spatula awkwardly nor trenching, lest your hands escape, and do not look too far ahead, lest you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound a vitriol poultice, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it so that the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the blood is stopped, then return to your work, until you have completed it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then look at your intended result to see if there are any small scrofulas remaining, if you cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if the boil has a great vein at its root, then it is not necessary to cut that boil in its root, but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall away by itself without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound to old cotton dipped in Egyptian oil, then the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cure the scrofula, then it is necessary that you gather together the two lips of the wound, and sew them up now, so that there is no longer any excess remaining due to the great size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	so it is necessary that you understand how to cover the root of it, and pull tight, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those boils that have superfluity, puncture there where it appears more.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and puncture it in the same way as the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then apply poultices with oil and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment to the raw flesh until it is healed.
de squinance	From shrinking
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old ones said and spoke of the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and that is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	It is necessary for those who have swallowed that the cut in the throat which is called "epiglote" should be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one does not help by doing so, because all the veins and the patient's major blood vessels are inflamed in those who have an abscess in the mouth or throat or in both testicles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the body, it is necessary to cut off the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglote, that we cut it below three circles or four a small incision across, between the two circles or according to the size of the incision of the syphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and it is so necessary for the cutting of the epiglote that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough to drain.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to its full extent, then cuts the leather until it comes to the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid shedding blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the superficies, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the splitting of the gum of the gallbladder which bursts through the broken joint and by the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leaves the open wound for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour is passed that causes doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound of the jaw, and sew all the way to the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Abacus says one does not do this just yet until the throat is entirely stopped up, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the default leads to failure.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is preserved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and therefore the ancients command to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four; then they command to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maid take a knife, and she thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the veins of the throat.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was summoned to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that she had not cut the vein nor led forth but the throat, and the veins were flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and stitched the wound, and cured her until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and it happened to the maid that she lost her voice, and returned afterwards to her normal state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the greenish-yellow color, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and it is according to two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	naturals, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	it has no natural contrivance
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident is according to two manners, of which one is similar to us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it has fear, and does not need to work on making fires except in that which is small, and examines and searches all the internal parts;
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it just like in a wound, and cannot be helped by any means, then cut it off, as one cuts off the nose, and treat it with all its contents, if there are any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and examine well everything, and cure it as is proper, until it is completely healed.
des nous	of fat
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of wounds, all of which I will say are similar;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I tell the whole difference that is between wound and abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that warmth and fever persisting, until the ebullition is past, and the purging is complete.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then the fever and warmth subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the nose having neither warmth nor fever nor pain, and containing pus which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a jellyfish, and becomes swollen.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, either fat or moist, and much colored as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of fat, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", according to what its form comes or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses of the nose is that you take or find the most moist place in the abscess, and turn your two pokers back and forth, until you know that the instruments have pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the obstruction, and take care lest it jumps again.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture constricts the cord, whatever its color may be, so treat it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after extracting the obstruction there is no moisture, know that it is fat, then treat it thusly in a cross shape, and take hold of it with forceps, and scrape it lightly on each side and watch the edge where it lies so you can lead it out safely with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot draw it out safely, then cut it into pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, then it will return through many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if even a small part remains and the blood teases you, then fill the wound with some caustic powders, and compress the wound, and put on soothing things, hot abscess, and cure it with other remedies until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is great, then cut off both lips of the wound, and treat those who have been injured flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the vein beats against you or another, and in your hurry and stress, you break off the lead of vitriol, and let it lie two days or three, until the wound has healed, and rest the boiling of blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to closing what remains of the wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	Behold the forms of the entrails mixed, and they are of three manners:
grans et moien et petit;	great and middle and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are of three manners:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	great, middle, and small, in order to surround the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which one sews sorcery, and they are of yellowed earth, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are most tried by black lead to encircle the ravens of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the pores.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the onyches are many in semblance, as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	large, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the onyches have two ravens of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if the onyches have three ravens, and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if the onyches have two ravens, and onyches with only one raven, and are of three kinds;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these things is that one cuts, and there are some who do not cut more than halfway, from which we strip the flesh, because one does not reach the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and of these intermediaries are the apertures replied in sleeves, so that the patient does not feel a thing when opening abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and middle-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use more than in a well-warmed place, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and in similar places;
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling scissors for flax, according to this form, by which one stops bleeding:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that bleeds at the puncture of veins and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Breast swelling occurs in some men when they begin to be corrupted, so much that it seems like a woman's breast.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, should treat according to this form until the line .b. to .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and pack the wound with medication allowing for some flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound by suturing, and care for it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the breast hangs down and is softened because of its size as it is in women, then cut it into two sections above, with two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is attached to the other at the end of each and contains the smaller line according to this form from line .b. to line .g.
