puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, as long as it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully closed, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the decomposition of blood, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it so that the remaining and fat can melt away, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses in the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the buttocks are types of hard scrofulas or boils, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and care for it with ointment suitable for this purpose until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, then make it as we have said in scrofulous cuts, and if the wound bleeds pus, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, then many times abscesses come to be, and so also happens with the vein inflamed and abscessed.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows this when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep inwards.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it to your fingers, then you feel its straining;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then it is reason to flee away.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolishness to cut this abscess, and similarly when it is under the armpits and in the groin and at the neck and in many other places, and it is very great.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary therefore to shun the iron treatment, and he who is at the head must also shun it, and in that which is on the swelling of an artery, one makes a cut above the long leather.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then perform the incision on the skin, and depart the artery gently from the flesh, until it is uncovered.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then put a needle under it and make it pierce to the other side, and hold the artery with a doubled thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then point to the place that is between the two lines of an instrument so long as the blood flows out which is there, and loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then administer the treatment until the bandage falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then heal those wounds suitable to this, until they are sound.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	And if the abscess is caused by the size of the vein, it is necessary that you take what you can from the abscess to all the skin, then insert the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess, as I told you, or tie one end of both parts to the two heads of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the threads will not come out, then reinsert another needle into all the thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut off the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut off the superfluidity of the wound and leave what is connected.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then administer treatments of tents and ointments until he is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses come in an artery and a vein, abscesses of the nerves come when they are wounded or from excessive hard work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often at the joints and in the hands and in all places where there are joints, and it is grievous abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one constrains him strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depth of the body, but below the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it is well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor underneath or above, and the one who is in joints must not be cut with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance I shall see contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is on the head or forehead, makes the skin at the armpit.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, one should grasp it with forceps and cut its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, one should suspend it with an incision, and scrape it, then cut out the abscess and put together the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	At times it happens in bellies and not elsewhere so far as I know, and it is a disease that is called "fung" by the resemblance to mushrooms, and has subtle roots and a large head.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are some small ones and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, with a small root, and split open and ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I coped them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 Z., and the work of incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the arthritic area is white and moist and of fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If he coperets with a spatula wide, and be in your presence the fire cauterization.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For when cutting comes many great discharges of blood, and if the blood flows too much, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made flax thread, and bind the arthritic area as we have said, and let it be for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then restrain him, and do not cease to strain the flax thread until he copes with the arthritic area, and let it feel his work.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	And if the roots are thick, then there is fear of cutting into the belly itself because of the wind, but you can well cut off the middle part, and then cauterize so it does not regrow;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cure the wound, and take care that you do not cut off the navel which is of a faint color and poor sense and with no regard for milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the care of ulcers later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the bread is burned
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the abscess comes from a cauterized wound or fissure of syphilis and is on the belly and in some of the boils, as it happens in other wounds, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the wound of syphilis and from the issue of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and openly shows its various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is because of the opening of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when one presses it at its sides it swells up, and then returns, and by chance it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance to the bath and from excessive labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it's because of moisture, it's a light thing, and you can see clearly when you press it with your hand, it doesn't resist at all.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it's because of blood, and it becomes apparent by these signs the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it's because of windiness, it is swollen when touched, and the works are such that you look to see whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery, or a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowels, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his anus, and be extended straight out, then sign in every direction around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then instruct him to sit comfortably between your hands, then go around the spot that you have signed with all the spatula, then cut off half of the abscess above to the great incision.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie around it with a strong thread or a cord of firm silk tightly, and the knot should be well secured.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work on the middle of the abscess extended over the thread, and press your finger's indication, and pierce the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it taken from the thread, then loosen it, and push the intestine further out of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bulge, then take hold of it with a forceps, and remove the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein is against you, go around it well, then return to your work and take two needles, and tie two thread pieces, and tie the two needles around what you have done in a cross shape as if you were piercing.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then strain the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave it to drain as much as possible, and let the dead flesh be separated by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	ou you cut when it is subtle and porous, then cure what needs to be done, and leave the abscess as we have said;
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what needs to be done, and mend the joint.
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division about the likenesses of gangrene, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid iron treatment;
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and we say that gangrene develops in the bones, and great caution is needed in the treatment, and the ancients say that when gangrene is in a joint or can be removed like gangrene in the breast, or in the armpit, or in similar joints, one should remove it all when it begins;
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is great and old, you should not approach it, for I never saw one that could be cured;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	None were ever healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient with black cholera sometimes.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	Then make him well if he has apparent fullness, then have the patient in good condition to do the work.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	Then wash your fingers or chance, and shave all over, and scrape off all the hair leaving nothing.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or anything, and if the bleeding makes you opposite to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat another wound until he is healed.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure that is done by medicine, and that which is cured by fire.
si est eclites soulement;	only enlightened
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch with iron in these two cases:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	it is to know, tympanites and hyposarchy, for it is a deadly thing;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	so when you medicate this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" in medicines, and the cure does not profit, if look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, as also distension of the belly and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if one must not touch with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is not too young nor too old, so you must thus proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	lift the patient straight up on your hands, and have the attendants press on the belly by thrusting water to the lowest part of the stomach, then take the spine-mold according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be split into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	at the tip, and even if it is not so deep that it can reach the intestine when one inserts it, and cannot hurt it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look to see if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary, then you must cut above the mouth of the third day on both sides under the armpit;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, then your incision should be on the left side of the mouth of the third day;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to dropsy, then it should be on the right side, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on top of the incision so that the superfluities do not flow into that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and plug it, and lift your hand to all the fat between the skin and the shank just as when cutting to the quantity of an ear or around it;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the sac as long as the pus comes out at its natural flow, and this is the sign of water, then take it away, and put that instrument in which there is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a thin silver chain, and it is made of light iron or archaic lead, and has a small depression in the part below.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three depressions;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on another;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is the key cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision which the writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top above is the almighty, so that when the instrument comes to water, it now descends on the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	then empty then the half or the third part, because if you empty more than is needed at that hour, by chance the patient may die from the release of his spirit from the arm, or he falls face down, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to empty space as the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtue signify, and their hairs;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the instrument and hold the water, and it is held now because of the key that stops the perforation which is above the siphac, for which I spoke, so you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then begin the instrument again the next day if you see the patient suffering those things and take out a small quantity of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this for some days and beware of pouring in until it no longer remains but just a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt about the patient and leave out a lot of water, if the remedy of burial or sand is hot, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and if it becomes discolored to drink;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and treat with drying medicines until he is healed, and apply a fire cautery to the stomach, liver, and spleen after extracting water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the flow
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without a perforation in the penis, or if it is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If this is so, then let it be done at once by piercing all the way through to the very small and subtle part according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then place the patient in a pit or hollowed out space with a subtle layer of mud, and bind him and keep him thus for three days or four, and when he wants to make water, have it opened up and let him urinate, and then replace.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance it does not matter, for the urine that comes forth will not allow it to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	That of which the pit is small, if it has medicines from a piece of lead, as we have said, so it will spread.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have a perineal opening in their place are afflicted, for none are born with a perineum at the head of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift up their penis first.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they are unable to relieve themselves because the material cannot come out just to the marriage line, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on his back, with the head of the instrument and the tip also like the size of a quill, so that the point may be in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and take care to prevent the flowing of blood which often occurs, and if it does occur, stop it with what stops bleeding, and heal the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times these blisters come on the instrument, and there is an ugly appearance of flesh.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and among them some are malignant and not malignant.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	so it is necessary that you take them up with subtle vinegar, and scrape and clean all of them, then put on moist Egyptian oil.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure him with divine ointment until he is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of poor color and foul-smelling, then you must apply a cauterizing agent.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have cut it, and the skin on the shaft is in the flesh and has part inside the peel and part outside, then you must remove the skin that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is sewn, then you should cure what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you cure it all together, then the head of the shaft is not assured that it will not be pierced, and there comes blackness and corruption in its shaft and around.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	so you should remove everything that is black and corrupted, then smear on it a plaster made of honey and flour that has been prepared from the bark of green pomegranates and vetches, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there comes bleeding, so administer the lunar cautery in this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cauteries are helpful in two dispositions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	to wit, for the evacuation of blood and for corruption;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you put a leaden tube or guide on the penis, and have the patient urinate through it.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the foreskin is inflamed at the head of the penis which has not been circumcised, or it has been caused by a wound or abscess, then it is necessary that you cut away with the curved instrument, until the adhesions are loosened and the head of the penis is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if this is a grievous thing to remove them, then it is necessary that you cut away with the spatula or some small instrument at the head of the penis and foreskin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then wash it gently between the two, and put a soft linen cloth soaked in cold water on it, so that it does not become inflamed again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a breaking of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	However, whenever we do this work of our own will and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most gentle for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not speak of circumcising their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen that the majority of masters and nobles who performed circumcisions around me were strong, and all young.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	So it was that the skins parted because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts above and leaves the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Then it is necessary to cover it up, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is done below the skin, the tip of the member is not ensured.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and at the cleansing of the ulcer by chance the iron escapes and the work is ruined, and many times such things happen that there is no need for cleansing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with force to all the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	When you press your hand, make it equal all around as much as possible.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread be well stretched around the skin.
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first operation is that you make the child think, if they understand, that you are only making them wrap the thread around the penis as little as possible, and then let it hang in all ways you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then make it stay between your hands straight, and bind the force between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand on the penis and blow or cut, and draw it up so that the foreskin of the penis is retracted.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then cleanse it well from the filth that is assembled there, then bind the foreskin with a double thread, then bind under one ligature and another.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it thus by the second ligature at the pouch and the left index, and tie between the two ligaments, then lift the key above hastily and train the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow a little bit by bit, for it is the mothers;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on top and on the powder I glue it with a yolk of cooked egg, tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh olive oil, and leave it on until the next day, and then treat another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The forms of forces to purification are thus:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two chisels should be held and biting, and the chisels also as great as the thumb in equal measure:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	the error of purification is when the keys inside flow out through the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Then you must extend it to your finger, as long as the swelling makes an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and file it evenly, and if you cannot hold it to your finger, then grasp it with pincers, and then file.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they last three days, and what is below the swelling is inflamed, then leave it so that the abscess is appeased, and scrape it lightly.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	and file as you can move, and keep away from the part of the shaft, lest it cause no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Then cure the swelling with sudden wound powder, which we have said or treated in dealing with powders, and if you file too much beyond measure, and it goes above, then it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to constriction of the kidney, or blood being frozen, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the kidney which is swollen or inflamed at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and let them be placed on the back, and stretch his belly from above to the back, and strain the patient's urine as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to express the kidney above, whereby the urine is released;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer an extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", which has this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be a thin, light-haired comb, like the feathers of a bird.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the thread be one and a half palms long, and fine at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of extracting urine is that you take a doubled thread, and tie it at the top to a piece of wool or cotton, and push the top end of the thread into the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut off the excess of the wool and push it just to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and a little hen's egg white, and make the patient sit on the seat, and lift up his bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil, and stale water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently place the syringe in the penis, so that it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upwards towards the mouth.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then insert the syringe before the bladder, and let the patient feel it coming up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide that goes there is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then pull out the thread bit by bit and little by little, and let the urine follow the thread, then pull it out further, and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and reinsert the syringe until the bladder is empty, and soothe the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When bleeding or blood comes into the bladder, or corruption is gathered there, and you see it distilling waters and medicines, then make all the instrument that is called "clepsedre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	She is closed, and if there are three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the hairs of the wick are trimmed so that the medicine does not overflow well without addition, if one can draw out the moisture and insert as needed;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see your medicines flowing into the bladder, put the head of the key in the moisture, and draw on the one who is within;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you draw out the moisture from the chest, and then quickly pull out the draining tube.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moistures enter in, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the subtle form of the enema by which one enemas the bladder:
si est ci:	if it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it's of silver or archaic, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below that is the breast or where the cord falls;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you use to enema the bladder, then tie it between two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pipe that contains this moisture over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the head of the enema in the urethra, then strain your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has been released, so that the patient feels that this moisture has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a nail, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it in the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do just as you have done with the bladder, press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	Of stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said the difference between a stoned kidney and rainwater, and all signs, and in which stone one should work with a file;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it's a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it opens up a hernia, and causes the patient's member to ache, and it pierces many times, and then swells.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and many of these stones bring forth foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is easier for children to recover until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in old men, and is in middle age, to those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and the cure is more light for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient by cleansing, in order to draw out all the bad humors that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it sometimes blocks any inquiry into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and turn him over and move him downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes falls from its height.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands be under his buttocks, so that the bladder is entirely declining downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then search for it and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in its place, then hurry now to cut on the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield to the touch entirely, then moisten your two fingers with oil from your left hand, if the patient is feeble, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and complete.
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and push it to its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, then draw it up to the navel of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press upon your finger, and push it out as far as you see where to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the attendant to press on the bladder with his hand, and command him that he stretch forth with his right hand the testicles above, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the incision.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I insert the spatula-like instrument, because this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And place it between what is between the crevices and the foundation, not in the middle but beside the left edge of the nave.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and your two feet should be at the foundation, and be the shape of the traverse so that it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	in case the pressure makes the foot at the foundation jump away without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there are stones with angles and margins:
si est griés a issir;	so it is grinded to come out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there are some that are worn down, resembling a gnat, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	To that therefore where it has angles and margins, make the shape larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then you must stretch on the pincers which are like a file at its head, in order to strain the stone so that it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you insert below the ly instrument subtle curved at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot bend it thus, then widen the little hole and if the flesh is stripped away, then bind with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there are more than one stones, then insert the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then remove it thoroughly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it must be cut away, and make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or his urine comes out again on the other side where the wound cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but always force it to be drawn or broken with pincers, until you draw it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, so anoint the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it tight, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then bind the patient on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, then arise the flesh with oil and water very well; then care for him with diaphrenic ointment and basilicon ointment, until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come to the wound and ulcers, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by this, which is known in such a way that without surging with urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	then pour out your bile into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and harm.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then wash the wound with water, vinegar, and salt, and aid him in all ways you know, until he is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the works you do to cure him, that you bind his two hips together, and put the medicine in its place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the penis, and stuck inside, and the urine cannot come out.
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	then cut it as I say, cutting many times, and excuse the cutting for this remedy.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod in the shape and form, with three angled tips fitted into one socket:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take a thread and bind it around the penis below the stone, so that it may not come down into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then insert the forest (i.e. a thin stick or reed) into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the forest in your hand back and forth on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then the urine will come shortly, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	So is broken, and jumps forth with urine, and is healed the patient.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	And if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then take a thread and place one end under the stone and the other above, then make the rod meet the stone between the two threads, then pull it forth, and free the ligament, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal him until he is sound.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It often happens that a stone becomes lodged in women, and if it does so once, then the treatment is grievous, and it is prevented by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perchance the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a well-known woman who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth manner is that the bone of the woman's arm is more prominent than the bone of the man's arm, for which it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity requires this, you should take a woman well knowing, and find one, and if you do not find her, then don't bother to look for another subtle midwife;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and the present one is a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands her to do what you command regarding the incision of the arm;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to strengthen her back or foundation and search for the bone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if it is true, then constrain it below its due and recommend to her that she must hold her due or with the patient and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder strongly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	and if it is true, then it should be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the cord, where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move your hand above or below the stone, and be the first to cut at a small size;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then press the rule in the cut, if you feel the stone so deeply in the wound that the stone can come out freely, and know that many types of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	it is to know, small ones and great ones and rough and smooth, long ones and rounded, and those with reins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the wound bleeds, then put a bit of vitriol powder on it, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is exhausted, and have tools that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the wound bleeds, and it's from an artery that has been cut, then put powder on the spot and tie with tents and bandages, and do not start again until it has stopped bleeding, and let the stone be and do not try to remove it, lest the patient might die by chance.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the swelling subsides, then return to your work until the stone is out.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rhemaces are nothing other than a collection of moisture or white leprosy, which is under the key of the testicles, that contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the web of an egg, if one thinks that this is another egg;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the scrotum between the white syfac that we said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and this does not happen unless one is not.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramification is from weakness that comes to the womb, and it spreads out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the scrotum, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it's declining to yellowish, or it's without red, or black, or aquous white, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is in the white syfac that we said, then it is the abscess reopens, as long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the scrotum, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper web, then it is the abscess reopens with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it's another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white scrotum, he will know it well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, test it with all the surrounding quarter-circles, because the form is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the quadrants, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cut it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be cleansed according to their strength and the replenishment of their body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then bind a cloth around his back, on something about a foot high, and put many cloths under it.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then sit on his left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on his right side, and stretch out the probe to one of the two groins of the scrotum.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula left-handed, and cut the skin of the scrotum between it and the long one down to just below the foreskin, and make a straight incision cutting through the skin of the scrotum just up to the white scrotum, and scrape out subtly according to their strength.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the syphac with water at the large perforation, and extract all the water, and then put in your probes, and stop up the syphac above.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the key of the stones, but only the syphac;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	cut it out altogether or in pieces, namely the coat of his subtlety, lest if you do not cut it well sufficiently, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the egg jumps out of your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work on the syphac;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then assemble the two leaves of the key of the stones with a suture, then treat it as you would other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the haemorrhage of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then strap the womb to all the suspensory, and extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if the water is gathered in two parts together, know that they are two roots;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then strap the other part similarly to how you did the first one evenly, and clean the wound, and put a moist compress in olive oil on the sore;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another moist compress in wine and oil on top, and place the two wombs on top, and place double cloths above, and tie it all up with a cord according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and put woolen threads in the same manner and have them sewn together into the armhole of the undergarment, and one of the straps takes up the foundation to the back, and the other to the part of the shoulder;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two heads on the two angels, and let everything be assembled into the restraint of the bowstring;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and sometimes medicine is applied to this cauterization in place of iron cutting, and it is that you take the cauterizing knife, subtly cut the skin around the testicles, and be heated as we have said, so that the white fungus containing water becomes visible;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	so take the cauter according to this form, and pierce that fungus once, and scrape it with this subtle hot cauter;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut it in all ways you can, until you have removed everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and be sure the fire does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more safe;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and be careful about the flowing of blood, and beware the works of cutting;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing makes you contrary, whether abscess or bleeding or other thing, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horribleness, then administer a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well assured by the signs we have said that the vein is good, make the patient sit on a light siege;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	then pierce the abscess in the part beneath all the spatula-like area, and put the perforation through the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and make the wound large so that all the pus flows forth;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and let the remaining pus flow forth, then cure it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not let water come out of the mouth of the wound, then it is necessary that you put a feather or instrument used to treat dropsy in this way;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound and know that the water comes back, and is assembled after six months or around, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the cutting of this reed there are many fears and dispositions, why it seems to me that much is lost if one lets it go.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say then that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the groin;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is through great chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive acidity and bilious humor that spreads to the groin or from striking;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and finds no pain, and it is a severe abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there are grievous and pitted abscesses, of foul color, and sometimes come from a wound in the artery, or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by a wound in the artery, it is known by the warmth of the abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not become necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	He who is afflicted with an inflamed vein is known by its appearance at the expression of touching with the fingers, and can well make the incision on this resemblance, and on other similar things;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and you should cut the key of the swelling, then lift it upwards, and pull out the white ligament, and release the suspensory from all parts of the swelling.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the wound is already sore with new scars, then it is necessary that you treat the wound, and the swelling.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is angry at the spleen or in those things that are inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you release all that tension and the swelling afterwards.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the joint is at the back, then it is necessary to cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, and care for it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a berry bud, with the softening of the skin, and the patient becomes very sick when it bursts.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the cure for this disease is just as fearful as the one before it, and yet we will tell you how to do it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You should make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then tie the suspensory of the skin down to your thighs, at all the vessels that are near the pubic area, and take hold of them, and stretch them out strongly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut the sponge trenchant wide at the crossing point near the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then fix an awl where there is the doubled thread, and tie it to the first location where the vein came out, and tie it again at the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then cut them in a straight line, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moles.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then treat the wound as with others that begin in the bowel, so that no vessel bleeds that nourishes one of the kidneys;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	For by this there is not harm coming, and if all the vessels come to view, then it is necessary to draw the kidneys in relation to all the vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	So that the eyes do not lose their nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and are unable to be helped.
