puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the assistants should squeeze it together with both hands as long as it is fully full, then extract the clyster, and lift the patient's legs up high, and if the medicine wants to come out, so hold on as long as possible.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps all night again, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge in a disease of windiness of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, then let the clyster be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the subtle form of the cystic swelling above which the skin is strained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or with a lance or bow or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or those that are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head that are simple, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it's from striking with stone or similar things, and although the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you are lightly doubting of hot aposteme:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	If he makes it so soon heal from the head wound itself if it comes out with blood from the wound, and the wound is healed on the opposite side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and instruct the patient to drink full of wine and eat big meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, then his meat should be thinned out and he should not drink wine or eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes to it, a moist cloth soaked only in rose oil or in wine vinegar.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if it is fresh and still has all its blood, and it is not affected by air or moisture, which I will say more about shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the ulcer has been moved by fire, then put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, so bring them together by suturing, as I will say about belly wounds, with suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is discovered to be in the bone, and penetrates, and holds only by a little, then cut it.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	Then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat, also like pigeons, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten flesh and it's not touching the bone, then cut off all the rottenness, and empty it out, then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if he has an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stanched by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and you put this powder that sets it so as the fire has changed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of this powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take a part of incense;
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	take three parts of living coal, and powder it subtly, and fill the wound, and bind it firmly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then tie it well, and let it stay untied, if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one does not do this with coal alone, except when one has no incense nor dragon's blood, but only when the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has changed the wound, indeed so it is, then do not put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put some digestive ointments or polts made of wheat flour, water and honey on it, until it flows freely;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then continue with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone breaks with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a hernia, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and put nothing restraining on it, because it harms the hernia and makes it retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and put nothing cold on the wound, because the substance of hernia is cold, and its continuity is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be soft, like chalk washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and wash the wound also in sweet water, and other minerals according to this manner, and moist anointings.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut and bind with bandages, then treat until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and she is bald and full of pus, then pierce or cut lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is severed, and blood flows forth, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize as necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is severed, or the trachea, and the conduit is preserved, because the flesh will go forth, then cut the throat above the cane of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it to its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then restrain it properly, and let it be for some days, then cure it with ointments as long as it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then cut it out.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all you can, and those that you cannot remove, let them remain until the wound is purged, and the issue is opened and loose.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, powder on powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it's a wound from an arrow or sword, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are any signs of festering that the patient should be alarmed about.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it's not deep and it's fresh with all its blood, then don't put any powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it up by the blood that doesn't flow forth, but rather let it flow back to the heart, and kill the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I apply an attracting unguent, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you don't have unguent, put old cotton in the wound to absorb any moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor evil trembling of the heart nor unnatural convulsions;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it with poultices and other treatments, until he is healed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal or produce pus, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is done as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or on the arm or back, then cure that which is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is large, by suturing;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, by powder; and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, then close the wound, and treat the parts if they are separated.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not cleansed, then let the wound rot, so it will ease the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the great wound sometimes the intestines or the membranes of the intestines burst, which causes the introduction of pus.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the suturing is more troublesome, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the great one, therefore one should insert the intestines gradually, rather than inserting them suddenly.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, and so they enter more gradually, and therefore it is better to move the medium wound, because one should return the intestine to its place as with other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the hernia of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common forms occur in the hernia of the belly, and the wound of another part of the body and two other proper forms are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and yet they are more proper with the hernia of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine comes out, and a gentle thing is needed to restore it, this is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak an esponge or cloth in lukewarm water only, or you boil it in water with squinat and cypress and spike, and apply the intestine until the swelling is removed.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and at times this wine restrains, and is necessary to remove the swelling so that it may be deflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling departing, then wash the intestine with water or broth and boil well, for by this means the entrance to the wound is prepared for little things.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make the wound a little larger with the instrument with which one cuts off hemorrhoids.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to cut away excess skin, so that no one should cut without great necessity there being.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut inside the curve and do not remove it, and see where the shape is.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps forth, set it back in its natural form to its proper place if you have the power, for this is a movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on his back and put his legs higher than his head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	et s’elle est in the part below the belly so sets the head and breast higher than the parts below and also if there is a wound of the belly in one of the two parts so sets one’s attention on what the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is fitting to remember what I say about great wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	Small wounds apply what is familiar to you, then take with your hands the poor minister who holds all the wound in his hand and close the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and it is the common manner of stitching, and that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound about two fingers' breadth, and insert a needle where there is good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two keys of the skin with the two keys of the slipper, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and tie together the two heads of the slipper fourfold.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then the strain of a double thread is wrapped around the needle's point on both sides, then the two edges of the wound are brought together properly, and then leave a gap of about two fingers' breadth, and put in another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then tie the thread of the cloth in the same way you did the first needle, and do not cease to do so according to what need you have of needles, until all the wound is restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and be the needles of suitable size, between fine and coarse, for the fine needles cut through all the flesh, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be of a suitable size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then bind the heads of the needles so they do not bother the patient at night; and I put tents or cloths on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and let them stay until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this manner of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it only requires one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second sewing is common, and it is that you join the two heads of the leather and the two heads of the silk together with a needle where there is a strong middle thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced all four heads together, then pull the needle through at the part where you started, in the way that one sews fabrics.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitching, about the thickness of a minor coin;
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitching is for men, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm's width large, and the intestines were torn two palms' widths long, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been gone for 24 hours, and the wound was closed 15 days later, and I cared for it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not heal him with oil, for I was in the region where one could not find it, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and placed gauze over the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and insert it from outside into the part that is inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the correct point in a straight line, then pull out the end of the siphon or cutting or where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce on the other side into the inside part up to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the furrier makes pelts, and that you leave once the siphon from one side and then take it up again on the other, until the stitching is entirely completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls properly, is such that some do, who join the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the ends to the other end, in this way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	thread an awl or needle nearby, and make a hole only in that place, and leave the two ends of the suture.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the awl, and make it pierce from the outside to the inside part, up to the two ends of the suture.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside part, in two other holes of the needle that are on the opposite side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen says this word, and others testify to it, so one should sew the belly with two needles, or there be thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is near the belly, then the incision is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if the heat has changed it, then you should return to the intestine and the flesh.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put powder in jamming charcoal, and if the heat has changed it, then put on some ointment that is at hand, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and stitch the thread, and sew up the stitches, and the gauze.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you don't have medicine, put this on, as soon as it starts to push out pus, old rags, and move it twice a day until it is clean.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not make a commonwealth to principal members, then it is necessary that you mix a little bit of lanolin in temperate heat oil or in rose oil, and put it around the wounds, and underneath the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or purging in the bowels, and many times happens, then cleanse with black vinegar, and likewise if the purging comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and probe within, and know that when it is the large intestine, then it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is because of the weakness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to those of natures.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the suture jumps out of the wound, then put it back in place just as the intestine is repaired; while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and turned green or black, then you must bind the place that is black so that no blood comes from there, because there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then tie what is between the ligature, and place the two knots below the wound until it is full of blood so that the extraction may be eased when the sutures fall out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some men, because I have seen that a man was wounded in the stomach by a spear.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and in it there was discharge and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I will the patient according to what I can, and did not cease to subtlety until he was cured, and the limbs were set.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the patient might have harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take fresh figs, then gather the lips of the wound together, and when the fig has opened the mouth, place it above the two lips so that it straitens its mouth above;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then tie the head, and it will remain so that he cannot untie it, then put another fig after in this manner as before, until the wound is entirely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	That intestine is adhered to the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the end of this intestine thread that is quite clean-shaven, and then bind it to the end of this thin linen thread, twist them together, and then push the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie it in a knot.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching is not other than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the groin's intestines, then there is no remedy nor salvation, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it begins to fester, is universally called a "fistula", and similarly when it breaks open and flows.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the natural nodation which is hard and white, or where one does not feel pain, and it is also curved like the feather of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes with a clear bow, and other times dense;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no scar, it is due to one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to know, by the slightness of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scarring inside and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much blood;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the flesh is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and is drained by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicine in the section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is necessary that I should make you aware of the treatment for fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the syphilitic, or from the intestine, or from the bladder, or from some of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs in the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are like this are of grievous sanitation, and there is nothing but hard labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is any fistula that does not come just to the place I said, and you have faith in the cure, and you know how to understand it, then take a tent of iron or earth, if the fistula is straight, so that you seek it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, then seek out a subtle punch, for the punch bends inwards around the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with tents, then cleanse it by one of the openings, for the moisture is so short from one opening to another, and purifies.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then ask the patient's consent to let blood at your discretion, knowing if there is bone or nerve, and be careful not to probe too deeply, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the corrupted flesh and the rotten humors that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure should be continued until it is healed; and if the fistula is well opened in its proper place, you should fill it as full as possible with moist compresses in medicinal poultice, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then you put on plasters in a good manner to healthy flesh, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healed by this means, then you should cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then you should cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If vein or nerve does not grieve or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then you should clean it until all the corruption is removed, then treat with things on healthy flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not cleansed, and returns to its previous state as before, know that you are not yet fully healed:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if you uncover and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore its place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus cleansed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep-rooted, so you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to rely on nature alone;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can draw it out with pincers, then draw it out with an instrument suitable for that purpose, and if there are many bones, then draw them all out, leaving none of them;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture hinders you, and there is no mistake or fear, then cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put a poultice on the wound that brings forth pus, and let it remain until the flesh is purulent around the bones, and then they will have more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a great bone, such as the leg or thigh, then remove only the corruption until all the blackened flesh is removed, then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupted flesh and comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so it is necessary to scrape and cover all up to the corrosion, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matters came out at the leg and became inflamed with a great abscess, and he had no reason to stop until it opened;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the physician through their foolishness worked so much on the abscess that it opened, and there was a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and many ulcers came that all burst forth with pus and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many physicians had treated him for two years, and there was no benefit in the art of healing, until I was summoned, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the ulcers with great corruption.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young person became red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one was coming against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	So I hastened and cut into one of the ulcers until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came as far as the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to be the corrupted bone and thought there was no other corruption except for that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to heal the wound with medicines over a long time, and could not close it.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found continuous corruption in the bone, and cleaned it, and then removed it, and was hesitant to close the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not until I covered about a palm of the bone with flesh, and made it whole to its entirety, then I healed it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to continue the treatment except for the patient's weakness, who could not endure, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because of the blood evacuation, it often happened that he was cured entirely, and instead of the bone, a hard skin grew out, and he had good condition and no harm or contrary to anything at all, neither in going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be set like this:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a linen, and strain it to the top of the exposed bone, and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	et place another thread of linen larger than the first one, and tie it above the flesh that is below the bone, and let it be so that you remove the corrupt flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above the joint where you see fat, lest it injure the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a tison or a table beneath the bone in order to cover up the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to uncover and see as much of the corruption as one can see and feel, and uncover again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place a tison beneath, and then uncover from one part to the other the corruption, and be sure of the length of the corruption as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and be on the other side where it contains bone.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there being no other angle to cut from.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the toe, it is very strong that thing, but anyway you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you can, but let the vein or nerve not hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisors and the sutures for cutting these bones are many, according to the structure of the bones and their appearance, size, subtlety, grandeur, smallness, and hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each instrument according to the appearance of the work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and knows that the work will show you the instrument with which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the instrument with which you have need, according to what it is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder can be dislocated either from within or from without.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicine to correct this corruption by the treatment of medicines, and it does not profit, then it is fitting to cover that member until the place where the corruption comes from, so that the patient escapes either by death or by the greater malice, which is more grievous, due to the failure of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the member becomes black, so it seems to be burned by fire, and afterwards it appears again, then this corruption of member spreads from member to member, and takes over the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten the cupping, and if it is due to the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the knee, then cup it, and do not give him space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, then cup at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cup to the shoulder;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the shoulder, it is a death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of his virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and so it does when the corrosion comes to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cup after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then cup the whole foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the leg, then strike at the joint of the knee.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the manner of striking or soothing the member is that you bind it above and below, stretching out one minister's line downward and another line upward, and you leave the flesh between the two lines to be cut one spatula width wide, until the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then strike or soothe, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the soothing does not touch the healthy part, and another lesion and abscess will ensue.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if bleeding comes from the wound when you work, then cauterize it quickly, or put some restraining powders on top.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it until it is sound.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to him at home in his bed:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he had a burn that seemed like fire-burning, and that corrosion came first to his heel of the foot, so it consumed all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that the corruption returned to the tip of his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him certain things that were reperfusing after the purification of the body, but he could not stop the corrupting;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I would not, for I had hope of reperfusing the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted whether if he cut his hand, he would not die, for the virtues of the human body were weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he was desperate all over, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and he healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I did not tell this story except for the reason that one makes another tale when it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes to a swollen part and stays so long that it gathers a great collection of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and pierce, and the pus jumps out, and the swollen part remains empty, just like empty vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin above is just as subtle as delicate draperies, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so elongated that it comes to the bone almost by front, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you scrape away all around, and similarly when it is subtle, just as one scrapes away curtains;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and is not hurt because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have faith that the skin is hurt, and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is full of flesh, then heal it with a poultice thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the breast is great, and the lump that is in it has a foul smell, then heal it with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take oil of aloe, and oil, and litharge, equal parts, and put it to cook in one vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take this mixture according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and make a poultice on the chest, and hold the perforation.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay for two hours, then strain it expecting;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleared, and the pus has been removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and at no time is it clisterized with ash water when this medicine is not present, and you should take ashes from the wood of the vine, pour water on them, then strain it, and apply it to the breast until you know that the breast is well cleared.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash water, then apply water and honey or where he has a little bit of litharge mixed in.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	You mix honey with wine sweetened, that the honey has the property to purify and wash, and the wine makes the blood fresh.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are sure that the skin is well purified, then mix with what brings forth flesh in it, and take definitive poultice, made with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	You apply it with some medications and ointments, whose properties I have said or treat the ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the pustule of the skin is small, and the plug of the poultice cannot enter it, then enlarge it slightly with a needle, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or Basilican ointment until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, so that it cuts and leaves only enough space for the poultice to enter, and if the pustule that drains pus is above, then cut or lower it down to its level.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Since the bowels are in harmony, do not let decay set in.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit, then prepare in such a way that the bowels run to the lowest place they can reach; since the bowels are in harmony, do not let decay set in and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see fit, then prepare in such a way.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowels flow gently downwards, and do not leave anything behind from the bowels;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative medications to put a seal on the wound, and place it on the linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the area with force in the wound, as it is no longer as wide as the first one; then anoint it gently with oil on another cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it on the wound of the breast to ease the bowels, and do not remove the great cloth elsewhere except after several days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is on the breast ulcer, often removes it to remove the boil, and knows what comes from the boil, whether it is venom or pus or enough or not digested or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that bursts forth on the breast ulcer, then know that the breast is already hardened, and approaching the state of health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, so change another dressing and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest ejects undigested bowels after many days, know that the chest is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, don't despair at all of one's health, for good health is near.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who take too long to clean their wounds with honey, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the undigested boil bursts forth from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not hardened;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	et if the skin is tardy in healing and is far away, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, as ointment defines it, for there is great part of vitriol, and this is the final medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined ointment and mix it with rose oil and equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then boil it and apply it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and make honey cooked and thickened, when defined ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then apply it to the cloth, and stretch it over the skin, and sometimes administer it to an Aristologist for a long time, and roots of lily, which is also like fine wheat flour and saffron;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simple or composite:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	crush them, and make powder, and put on the honey I said, and use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is inflamed and is not healed by this remedy, then know that corruption has penetrated deeply and makes an impression on the bone, or hardens the limbs, or tightens the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the wound is a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the joint
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb, or of the foot, or by chance arises in other parts;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and not attended to, then the abscess becomes gangrenous and runs and pours pus so long as it can run to the root of the nail, and by chance may even drain entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion all the way to the bone, so long as it brings stinky pain, and is the shoulder joint wide, and is the color flush.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the surplus flesh remaining from the boil, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleed, then it is necessary that you place the rod underneath the nail that pricks the flesh, and put it above, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicinal and corrosive substances in order to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with ointments until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it away, and take out the pus, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, he cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the joint corrupting, then cut it away as was said before, and treat until he is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and he feels great pain, then you should heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the gouty lump above with a diagonal cut, and be careful that the cut does not come all the way to the skin below the lump, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The joints that occur in the hands of some people by chance are all fleshy, and sometimes there is a bone or it has bones, and occasionally one is born at the root of the joint, or birth is in some knuckles of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born in any part of the night from the shoulder does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the shoulder, by chance moves.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is fat is light, in that way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born in the root of the joint is hard to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	it holds up from being cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or will be at the back part of the body, it is necessary that you scrape off first the fat around to the bone, then scrape the bone to a suitable thread for this, and then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The kind of wound that comes together by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cover this wound so that it can repair itself according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the skin is joined, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of its joints with the palm, then bind that wound as it is necessary.
des vils	wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are great swelled and inflamed, full of melancholic excesses, which come from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it occurs more in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you minister to him sometimes purging of gall, and then salve from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron cure is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is where you cauterize, and wipe away the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open a vein, and let it bleed completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The skin sores are according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	The first sign is a hot water swelling in the leg very strongly, until the gross blood becomes subtletized, then strain the patient's leg from above the hip down to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then cut the vein in one place or two places or three, with a wide incision, then lift and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure without harm.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and instruct him to eat flesh food allowing black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and purging when the veins are full, and it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The remedies for this are according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the patient's leg if it has many hairs, then put it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and fill the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you do not have a bath, then warm it by the fire, and then cut into the vein at the long part of the thigh or in the lower part below the knee.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cut open the skin at the incision, and scrape away the vein from each side, until it appears as it should when one feels it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and then you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then bind the thread below, until it is raised from the skin, and then incline it to the incision lightly, and then cut in another place above three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape away the skin above the vein until it appears, and then lift it to the thread, just as you did, and incline it to another incision, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	Then cut another size, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut at the joint of the foot, then train and lift just to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then strain it from size to size, until it is all free, then cut.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	And if you cannot strain and lift it, then put a needle on all the strong thread, and tie and train it, and put underneath the rail, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out.
