et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And guard that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then it cannot be strained or lifted, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	And when you have strained it all, then put a damp cloth of linen on the site of the wound in vinegar and oil rosated.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and curved together, and it is not straight, as we have said, so you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to open the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it opens the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is inserted into legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and on the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it may be found in another part than legs, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from beneath the skin, as it does inside the body of serpents and worms, inserted between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then the skin changes, and the vein begins to flow forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth one and a half feet long up to two and a half feet, and tie it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it comes undone at the back, so wrap it around the cloth again, and tie.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, so cut a part off, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it at its root, until it is entirely removed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, so it will enter into the flesh, and bring about an abscess and corruption in that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that she be treated little by little up to the top, and no part remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it often happens that this vein is treated up to ten or fifteen palms in length, and one man came to me whose was ten palms long, and when you cut it, so it bursts forth with a flow or a perforation, and pierces right through to the bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the matter inside be emptied, and bring to place medicines that have not been prepared for any day, then cure as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And at times to this vein many raindrops fall, and indeed when it opens in the joints of the foot or foot, and there comes out much pus, and then many raindrops;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Moors that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "beef sickness", because it often afflicts oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all around the body rising and falling, and the patient feels it well from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it is going, and jumps forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by purtification of some humors, such as come from worms and serpents and lumbri and ascarides or the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and one doubts of his evil because when it goes through the body and it climbs to the head and comes to the eye by chance it returns and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cure and pull out, one cannot avoid but when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong tightly tied ligature, then cut on top and pull out what protrudes, and if the tip is embedded deeply in the flesh and you cannot remove it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming up to the head near the eye, then press down below it with a strong seal, then cut on top and pull out what protrudes;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient with a cleansing of the body by soluble medicines for bad humors brought on, and beware of eating foods that produce corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and soon after, I saw it rising also like a worm on the shoulder, more quickly than anything, just as hot silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after it ran all over the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that it was turning around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how she moved from member to member in this way, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had wanted many things to move well from one place to another, but I did not want it, just as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and her veins uncovered, and therefore that apparition appeared constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason to those who are plump, and who have moist bodies and veins responsive.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind above and below hastily, and then cut on top until that constrained ventosity issues forth from the place.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it to your eyes, so treat it with the remedy of those who calm the vapors, such as stinking pills and viper's pill, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of theirs is that there are some who have great points, small ones, hairy ones, and roughened ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those who have two angles, and those who have tongues, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls in any member, if it falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in principal members such as head, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, warn you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not warn you at all, and the arrow is not exactly out, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And when the brain sign appears when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the spinal cord that is above the brain is torn, it is when there is blindness and numbness and confusion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of gall.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and possibly it is without force from the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and possibly it impairs speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaping from the moist white wound resembling pustules, and also jumping like a bruise of flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, then take care of it and pull out the arrow if it's not stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hits the heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves as well as the hair, and in cold black blood, and comes with shivering and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death is impending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that strikes the spleen is when without any foam it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat inflates, and the patient's color changes, and sighs deeply and searches for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow hits in the covering of the liver, it is on the small ribs.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and vomits great bile and great pain and sighs.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and all the limbs of the shoulders are numb.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, by chance something from undigested food bursts forth from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly and bursts forth through the intestine route, there is no hope for recovery or in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow hits in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels very painful.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and back of the neck and rib cage and hip and knees and legs, and a similar limb, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it's not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you may do similarly.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	An arrow fell at home on the threshold of the neighbor's garden.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out and drew it under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And drew out an arrow that had fallen in the fat of the eye under the paper, and the arrow was bent back, and could only be retrieved as far as the point towards the fist, and the arrow was as long as a Turkish bow, and very light without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The eye was healed, and no bad accident came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled out the barbs, and extracted it slowly as I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw out an arrow from the man whose was shot in the belly, thinking that he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after having passed 30 days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out further, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see the man to whom an arrow struck his back, and the wound is sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and his natural dispositions did not change, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural activities.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another man, to whom an arrow struck his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And draw out an arrow from the king of the princes, who had been struck in his thigh, and was slightly declining to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and was the arrowhead fully covered.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was summoned to the treatment after she had fallen three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for her in every subtle tent and did not find her.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a pricking and pain beneath his right earlobe.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I put on the wound a plaster that is attractive and digestive, because the lump did not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the wound from the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on for many days and the wound healed above, and the patient remained that way for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead within his body one day.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on the wound medicine that is corrosive by many days, until it was open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which was stuck in the joint.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I inserted into the opening of the wound by this medicine's aid, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and exceeded the terms by about four months, and then healed so well that I put in forceps and pulled apart and couldn't get out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to subtilize and ingeniously devise various methods of instruments, until on the first day I got well-made forceps, according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as I was guiding it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctor judges that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was bound up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you set your care upon what I do not say, for books cannot take everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters know well to treat small things and what is present and failing, find nine remedies, and nine instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not emerge from members where they are stuck unless according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the way they enter, or by another place;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out far from where it enters is an arrow entering the fatty parts of the flesh, and sometimes this happens now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump out now, then let it stay until the fatty parts are gone around, and the exit is opened.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it's stuck in the bone and can't come out, then let it stay like this for some days, and move each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps; and if it does not jump, so pierce around all the way to the subtle forest, until the surrounding bones are widened, and then treat.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and goes just up to one of the bellies of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said occur to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if you do not extract it at all, but leave it until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow comes just to the sacrum, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come just to the skull, and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then persuade him to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is stuck in this way and cannot come out further, then administer tarre around, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut it so that the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears at which it is stuck, then remove the flesh that is stuck two parts away from where you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as far as you can, until you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be subtle that you do not break the arrow, lest you pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out at once, then leave it until the skin around it is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you disagree, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and think how you can pull out the arrow without danger, either soon or late, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him, for it is the greatest aid that can be; and if you cannot, then place him as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it appears to be near him, or the skin is swollen in front where one can see or feel apparently.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut on up, until the forceps can take hold, and then pull it out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for now and then re-start the extraction until it comes out finally.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrow is stuck inside him, soak his entire body in water;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrow breaks, and you have to administer binding, then administer the instrument shaved, so that the point of the arrow goes into the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push forward, and if the arrow is stuck, then insert the instrument with a pointed end into it to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you cut all around the flesh where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is stuck in the head or side or belly or bladder or ribcage, and it's nearby, you can cut on top of it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and take care not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then pull out, and then cut the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps with which one handles arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, moderate, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like that of a bird's feather, in order to push forward at the tip of the arrow, as it is shaped here.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the forceps to push and to grasp if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed oneself, of which there are 16 on the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two veins that are located after the ears, which are called "herbeches";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples appear;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspirations";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two sinewy things that are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the upper lips above the mouth, and they are called "augerich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins by which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and people commonly call it "the vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the median is called "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and people commonly call it "the vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the spleen is situated in the right side of the belly, and the common people call it "the vein of the belly", and it is located above the kidneys, and it is that which is cured, which becomes manifestly apparent on the abdomen.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the wrist and the ankle, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is under the armpit of the left side, and the second saphenous one that is at the ankle of the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nerve" which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The cure of the veins that are after the ears helps ancient headaches and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of a healer, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and stroke the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then bind the patient's neck with a strap, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent folds from the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and then at your discretion, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, so seize it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and push it down through the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand up along the entire vein above, and cut through the skin and the vein as much as the length of two fingers, and let out blood until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind it tightly so that it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The wound of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is worth migraines ancient and old, and sighted, and accustomed to ophthalmia, and in the course of hot tears to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the surgeon are such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that the patient stretches out his neck, so that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below your thumb, and then signs with nodding;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the key on the vein above your thumb index, and push the lancet down, and lift the vein up, and cut it, just as you have done in two other veins, and make the incision according to your necessity;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then place a cloth on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of their binding and extraction, in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The wound on the forehead vein is worth as much as the cephalic vein in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraines, and in headaches;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patient stretches his neck twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fossor", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press down with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is healed, and not once make a wide ligature.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it's not fitting that the flames be too strong;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the blood flows in a cross shape, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The juice of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and the acne, and the redness, and the yellowish coloration in the eye, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their juice are such that the patient strains his neck by twisting from some kind of bond, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the blood, and let it be like the traverse, about a finger's breadth long, about a span wide, because there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make a compress of blood, as much as you need it, and then bind it with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The blood of the vein of the night is worth as much to age, and also foreseen, and also diseases of face, so as emigraine and redness that comes on the face, and indeed when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the qualities of the blood are such that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose to the left hand side, and takes the subtle flame long, and puts it in between the lip space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start flowing now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not flow too much in front, and let the blood run according to your need, then bind it overnight, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two groins helps to narrow down the swelling, and at the beginning of flux, and many diseases, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and sores;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the sickness is that the patient stretches his neck from under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and the master is standing on top of the patient's head, and the patient sits on the stool, then opens the vein a little bit widely, then draws out blood temperately, or as long as it is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then does the other side on the other vein, then loosens the ligament, and holds it steady in the middle, so that the patient does not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leaves him until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bloodletting of the veins above the lips is helpful for bleeding in the mouth, and for corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and around the neck.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	and the quality of the sickness is that you have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn your lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is to the right lip and the other to the left, and they are known by this that they are black, and because around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	cope then one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, so cut the largest of each side, and do just the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healing beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding from the veins that are below the tongue helps greatly after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient takes a seat between your hands before the sun, and lifts up his tongue, and looks down at each side into one black vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep in, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	out of all fiery myrrh large, or olive subtle as cutting trenches, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are large and subtle according to the breadth and narrowing of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mirtin incision is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and full of thick blood apparent, and which contain thick blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive oil flame;
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and at the neck, and at the breast, and at the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to bind tightly and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great deal of blood comes forth, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and it must not be poking the flame, but cutting as with a shears.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open visibly, then you should extract it and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you take some of it away from him, or you let blood flow into his arm instead.
elle apert manifestement;	it opens visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut the flesh with a flame-like instrument, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you grasp the arm and touch the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a ring and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a flame-like instrument;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	Fix the wound then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flow upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood from an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your tourniquet on lengthwise, then remove it if the bleeding ceases, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	If the arm breaks, and let it be so, and do not move the patient's arm;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be on guard, and do not move the patient until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the blood is not staunched, and it flows, and medicine is not present to you, then compress the artery if it opens, for the head of the vein retreat.
et estainche li sans.	and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a membrane of fig bark, and hollow it out, and take one half and tie it on well to the other day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	If the blood stops flowing, it's fine.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then if you treat it with the powders that stop the bleeding,
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not guaranteed in many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the power of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The vein of the neck in a mixture so helps to treat blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be wary of the nerve that is below, and if he cuts too deeply, he will find the nerve, and it will swell and the bleeding will not cease, and by chance cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you must tie the arteries with anestil.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and shield the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the cephalic side helps, which draws blood from the head and assists the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed when pricking the flappy part of the olive or mint vein, because this is the most saving of all veins, for there are no nerves nor arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lighter spot, and do not trouble anything if it does not work the first time, and we start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance, some people's veins fill at the first attempt, but it does not trouble anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the pulse is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that bleeding is not done except to preserve health, and to prevent illnesses from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the bleeding be done in one of the three veins that are at the throat:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	To know, cephalic, swift, and basilica;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should be cleansed at the beginning of prayer hours in springtime and autumn after eating, when the signs of repletion appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should be cleansed on the first or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The cleansing that is administered for diseases has no fixed time, but whenever it is needed in the morning or at night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to cleanse children until they are 14 years old, nor a woman who is pregnant for less than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not heal those who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to cleanse themselves in whatever way, it is necessary that he reveals the intestines with a light enema, if they have many foul humors retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous substances harmful to the main members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	one does not heal well who is too full of meats, nor who is drunk, until he has purged himself.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one does not heal well after a violent passion, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequent staying with a woman, and travail, watching, and sleeping, and all that is contrary to virtue, or by something of war or of body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then adjust the humors, if the blood is thick, with meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter or take a bath, if nothing else prevents, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the wound around the third hour, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself that day from labor, and toil, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be seated and joyful, and let the surgeon stand higher than he who is being treated, and rub the arm twice or three times, then loosen the tie above in a gentle manner, for when it is too tight or too loose, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the joint with your hands until the veins swell, and one senses it;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the surgeon's cloth with a small amount of old oil, then place the tip of his left hand on that vein below the joint, about a finger's breadth where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not flee and fail from being pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee like strings from the surgeon, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts the cloth on it, the cloth retires, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is among those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, then is the wound too narrow, therefore it is necessary that the physicians be informed about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein works the first time, that's good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then one reopens it again a little below or above hastily if the swelling is not gone.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the swelling is gone and the patient is reassured, then one lets him stay for a day or two and does not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	in case abscesses will arise soon;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	nor does one enter water, then reopens the wound if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it will not flow as much blood as you see, then trust in that same opening to drain properly all the way.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and do the work with some haste, yet when the limbs are swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swollen, do not begin to bind it again, and apply a little bit of oil on top, for it lightens the body from blood, and is good for this limb as is the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each binding that you bind the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and the same is done with triangle and blue ointment, when it is applied to the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	so that the blood flows and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a great abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not bound more than once or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten, and apply a wet sponge to the limb in warm water and silk for a little while.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the bleeding from the vein, and if it stays at its place for some days with no blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on something with aloes or myrrh mixed with calaminth juice, poultice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there is abscess and swelling at the joint of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of your hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Be careful not to put anything on it of what we have said, for by chance the artery might be cut off.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make a plaster on it so as to harden the place, then apply another cure until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each blood according to its quantity and virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	If the blood is black, then let it flow out until it is red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, then let it be thinned out until it becomes subtle.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, then let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, to make the wound wider and the flaps larger.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and make it heal little by little, and one should make it heal by cutting across, not by piercing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing saves from the loss of blood and the compression of nerve, and is worth more than the healing of a long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give moist bread in apple juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is heated, treat him with blood three times or four; And if he has a cold complexion, treat him before the wound becomes wet and slimy in a sweet syrup, or in a scented honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and with well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he has palsy of the vein, after the issue of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks a decoction of charcoal and subtle aromatic syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to flex his arm and be healed another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to flex his arm after the first treatment, and he has a strong body, then he heals in about 7 hours after the first treatment, or around the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to be healed from another part, then he should be treated again on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood inside the body which is already heated, and it brings forth fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so that one must draw out a great quantity, and enlarge the aperture until it can be drained freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must reward all the conditions of health, and put your hand on his pulses when he is healing, lest death come in place of healing, and this happens many times, when the healers are neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary when you see the arm dislocated and bleeding again, and the aperture is closed, that you press strongly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is bent, let him straighten his arm quickly, for it would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let him leave it until he recovers the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you put the point of the flame to the tip of the vein until the blood that has frozen in the puncture flows forth, and put on a poultice of silk rewet in water, and press slightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, then let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein within the arm is treated at the location of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the scab is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then be bound slightly, so that the vein appears well, then heal now through the center, not through the width or length.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and be the puncture wide, and heal well near the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, then do not put my hand into hot water, for one puts it in winter rather than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this wound is more saved from all other wounds, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein on the palm of the right hand is worth more than all other diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand and put it in hot water, until the wound is drained, so that one may see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein goes awry, and you cut into it entirely, then nothing will hurt.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not cut too deeply into the bone, for the nerves are underneath all stripped of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the pus is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled out as much as is necessary, then put oil and gall on the vein to speed up the healing, and do this for each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The wound on the left hand is good against mouse disease, and do everything in the same way as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sickness of the sophene is worth to all the diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the qualities of his urine are such that the patient pours some water into hot water, and rubs on the vein so long as it bleeds, and above the jointure of the foot;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins going;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then take out the largest vein, or the one at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you take out the vein above the foot, then beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut across in a straight line as when cutting.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the edges be even.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the needle fails the first time, then repeat the second at a spot above, because the flesh is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus do the same to the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of strength, and its wound is good against the pain of the backside when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his urine is such that the patient enters the bath and strains above the knee four times by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then allow the urine to flow in all ways you can, and crossing over.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth moving than cutting, for the wound is sound, and it is very red to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then let the urine flow from any part of him that opens, or from the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let so much blood flow as you see, and then loosen the bandage, and put on linen and tighten it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Wounds of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Poultices are made from horns, or tin, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and wind-sweating is done according to two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this wind-sweating which is without wounding is done according to two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is done with full force, or without force;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and wind-sweating which is done by wounding and drawing blood is done in fourteen places of the body, where one is entirely on the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the ventoses under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the ventoses on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventoses above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the ventoses in both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the ventoses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the poultices of two ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the application of poultices does not concern blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore one should not weaken it too much, just as with bleeding from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not suitable that she be administered, nor in any fire or sense of fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases it is necessary to apply poultices, or for habituations, we should administer each one hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and in each season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have need to apply poultices, then have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are some who turn red with repletion and flush in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkness falls upon the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who spit out a drop of blood from their mouth, and have swollen the tongue, and redden with blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who dream, and see through blood and hurt and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sap of the mummy so helps with the grevously wounded head... that comes to the eyes, and it does not seem right that this should be after the evacuation of all the body's blood.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this purging is in place of the sap of the cephalic, and it does not seem right that one who is of cold complexion or has catarrh should use it, for it causes them very great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it does not seem right that the elderly in use it, nor those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from this often become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the leech a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The purging in the neck is in place of the sap of the head and of the brain, and therefore it is good for constriction of the stomach, and for rending the channel of the womb, and for all, and for fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	et it is necessary to force slowly, for if she holds too tightly, so one will encounter obstruction or indigestion or heart trouble.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The swellings on both sides of the neck are worth the pains in the head, and obturation and emigration, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is equal to the health of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you must instruct the surgeon to extend his hand when placing, not to cut the artery, and not to let blood flow excessively.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The swellings under the chin are worth mouth diseases and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is equal to the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The leechings on the shoulders are good for the disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The swellings on the sides are worth as much as three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins;
