et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to strike too deeply by fontanelle, for the bone is bare of flesh, and knows below nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the cupping glass be large and made of earthenware, so it may well draw out.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if she were subtle, she would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and it would make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping glasses on the legs so plainly heal, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains of kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and restore flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in place of the two shins and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and bring on paleness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The manner of applying the poultice is that you put it on first empty, and then squeeze it temperately, and apply it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease to do so until you see the red flesh appear and the blood well up.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then boldly, and replace the poultices, and take heed to the condition of bodies, for there are some who have dry flesh and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to wound once only, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and one a little deep.
et suce legierement.	and squeeze lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to wound twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to wound a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to let out a little bit of blood little by little, if it suffices just once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeat the process often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, then pierce it deeply, and make sure that the veins are perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have tough skin and hard, and who have large pores, that you anoint the soles of the adhesive plasters with open and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, with oil of wormwood, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, take bitter oil, or balsamic oil, or oil of anise, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if one's skin is tender and has large pores, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but rather wash after the leeching with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin seed water, or porcelain flower water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And that person who has much moisture, should rise easily with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive swellings drink old wine, or water of salsify, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or something similar;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and it is not necessary to heal with a poultice before bathing or bathwater, but after the bath for one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he does not sleep after the poulticing, and it is necessary that he be warned, when he should be poultriced and when he is poultriced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are sick choleric temperaments, and if their blood is too hot and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green grapes and endive and lettuce in abundance, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and tender meat, and flesh of capon, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, so take honey syrup and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and tender meat, and tender birds and small game.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and when he will gather himself, so must he drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men at times treacle or muscat before the sweating, or afterwards, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the sweat be fine, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The poultices that are applied without hurting are those that are applied on the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the stomach and the bowels and the kidneys and the loins, for these members do not suffer being hurt there, and one only does so to draw blood from member to member, as we apply them on the breasts when the milk runs.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply poultices on the stomach and on the bowels to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and stays the pain when there is inflammation or stone; so stays by its attractive virtue the inflammation or separates the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one places it on the liver and on the menses when there is retained windosity; and these cupping glasses are administered empty in order to suckle only so much.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and at times they are administered together with fire, and at other times plain water, as in the diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water only, or with water that has been boiled with herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the poultice administered at fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two and a half palms of perfunctory depth, and have or coat the surrounding area around the mileu with a small pit, as if to insert an awl, and be of iron, so soft beforehand that it does not wound the patient when putting it on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let it be with one hundred and twenty a beam of crossbow or iron, to put a candle in place, and there are many and small ones according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for children's poultices are different from old people's, and thin people's from fat people's.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus put this poultice on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the candle of wax or ointment, and put it in the middle of the poultice on the beam that is inside the poultice, so that the light may be at the bottom of the poultice that it not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and let it be on the boil that we have said, so that when you want, if there is steam, remove the poultice.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the ointment just as before, and continue to reapply it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass then which is administered to a patient with pleurisy, there is no stick nor pimple, and it is only brought out when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member as soon as.
et c’est li forme:	and that's the shape
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Cupping glasses are only brought out when used for members where it is not possible to put cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare bones that are denuded of flesh, like the head or neck, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find cupping glasses that are in clear and pure water without any perturbation, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in cool water until they are familiarized, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be healed by vein and by poultice, then rub the member until it is red, and put on bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clean and dry, and can be used to put a poultice, then one puts it there, because this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the limb by easy stages, and then by water, very well, and then tighten it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb heals too late after the application of poultices, then wet a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the poultice is congealed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the poultice is multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol or gall, and similar things, until it is congealed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the limb half of peeled broad beans, and let them stay until they dry to the limb, so it will stop bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more assistance, take other surgeons.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the surgeons do not want to take it, then moisten the wound with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the pus issues, and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will set.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are flowing, then powder with a little alum and vermilion, or ashes, so they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for fracture and desiccation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish men throw themselves away from this chapter, for they have never seen anything in the old books nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is estranged the science from our land, for I never found any good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing except by the science of ancient books, or that I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and through experience, and through the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and shortened it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that are provided, as I have done in these two chapters previously.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book, the summaries of words and chapters where wise men put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who have experienced it know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one side and another; if nothing else helps, such as weakness of the body, or infants, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the weather is not too cold, or too hot;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and also cold cholera, that is to say, cold fits, and the flesh of hare and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with flesh which fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about hot aposteme or expansion of matter in the member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient recovers to his previous good state which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to recover, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make a good nourishment, or he has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and belly of veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nourishment, the muscles are restored more quickly and the break is healed sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old and decrepit people cannot be well restored or joined according to their nature because of the decay of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but don't worry, reset on the broken bone with strong cords that bind and join the member together, until it is as strong as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and don't leave him without his work, and therefore he must be nourished with big meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break of the head is another thing than a break of the breast or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that occur by twisting, and others by bending, such as the cutting of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with all a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for every way, let him have his own device, and his proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory brings into its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the break of the bone is by twisting, and it appears well by departure, and sounds under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	et when there is no twistedness nor at the touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no point of breakage;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twistedness, or crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you must not move it by hand, but put on medicines that come after this, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breakage that occurs in arching, and are the two parts separated, it is necessary to put them back together evenly, otherwise abscesses will come to life there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses hotly come there, then let it be left alone for a day, until the abscess is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it equal to the movement that you can make lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this is more light than the restorations of those who have pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then restrain it, as it is fitting hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, two parts long, whether it is arm or leg, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	et set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are dislocated, then reset by all means the adductions in their places as far as you can, and take care that through your work does not come to the patient injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set well the two bones of the skeleton according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel by hand if it seems to you that it is not well.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	so that it be set well, and not strained too much, nor pressed as those who bring about apostemic heat and contraction in the member through their work, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is set right, then chastise the patient so that they do not move it, nor in waking nor in sleeping, nor in turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take care that the member be so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	When he feels no pain, except perhaps at the tip, it is necessary to put him in such a state that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that he be set straight, so that twisting does not occur when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and largeness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar things:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to envelop him with soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to envelop him with a wide and strong linen, because the wide linens encircle all the large member evenly, so that there is no defect.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then wrap it with light cloths, three turns or four according to the member, and hold your hand a little tight on all the linen, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break will move away a little from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften it gradually, little by little, until you take away a great part of the healthy flesh, then take hold of another ligament and turn around above the broken joint;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break and strain it moderately, not too hard nor too gently, as we said in the first lesson above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments strips of linen or cloths, until they are all even, then tie everything above with bandages, and then put your well-made straps on, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, then put something calming and hot on it that removes the swelling, and let it be like that for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then strain over your straps and let them be of the middle of a well-seasoned ash stick, or of fir wood that makes clubs, or of palm tree saplings, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the break be a little bit bigger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is needed for the member of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then stretch it on the splints just like you did at the first joint, then tie above with a thread conveniently, just like at the first joint above the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is stretched up, the looser it should be down;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and be of fine linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their bonds with cordage twisted in tortuous ways, and it's a great error, because the bond cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not need to have between each splint less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the points of the stakes after the straining in their own flesh, then put under them strips of linen or wool, so that he may not be hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the ligaments are broken, I will say the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to strain on all the members that are broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are great, it is not necessary to put splints more than after four days or seven, or more according to the security of abscess happening afterwards;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and here is the manner of ancient plasters to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that remains at the walls of the mill, and mix it with a great deal of egg, and put this confection, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of plaster restoring breaks in various conditions, and indeed for women and little children, for it is not either too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another manner of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	take aloes, ladanum, unguent, asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mix them in the proportion of ten to one.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Mirror and aloe, five ounces;
alechil VIIII З.;	Aloe juice nine ounces;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix with the white of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if a man's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it quickly restores broken bones, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is worth for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take muggite and muskavle, ten ounces;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mirror and aloe, nine ounces;
acaice VI З.;	Vinegar six ounces;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boiled Armenian ten ounces, and grind well, and mix with water or the white of an egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way of plaster for joints and bones that are out of their places, and relieves the pain happening, and they use it to shape the bone and the breaking:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new linen, and marinate it in vinegar and oil cooked, and place it on the sore.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore at all, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to plaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried leaves of fig tree and leaves of earthbound burdock, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to ease the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of Vismalve, Chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of poppy, each one a part.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and apply it to the members that are inflamed, or if it's not inflamed, mix it with moist water of coriander, or water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster even stronger than the first one, when abscessed flesh comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of Vismalve, and seeds of flax, Balaustie, Mellilot, and Sandwort, and flowers of violets and Chamomile, each one a part.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and crush, and cook with saltwater, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore it with anything more than a wax and oil mixture, and nothing else besides, and he says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on the broken member to restore it with dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to plaster that is good for wound and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mallow and hawthorn of men's heads, or feathers of birds, and marshmallow, and equalize them, and crush, and make a plaster and lay it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if you do not loosen it by main days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light linens, and moist sea sponge, and plunge it in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it up with a nut, until you are certain of no hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and may the pain be removed, then resume the subtle bandage, and apply a little ointment, and do not strain it as hard as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is gone and redness, pain, and swelling are all removed from it, and you need to use ointment and bandage again, then resume, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the member, then do not remove it until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the splint is secure and approaches the union with the flesh above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and let the swelling of his meat increase, as I said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the place drying out more than is necessary, know that pus cannot come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then bring forth hot water mixed with vinegar, every time you loosen it, and let each third day pass, and slightly relax the ligature.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work, then cut off the pus from the member, and quickly do what foolish physicians do, who leave the member twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and it is poor work, and I see nothing else but to tire and toil correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various types of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of breakages and diverse shapes, and the causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are breakages that are caused by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone takes out all the bone just up to the shaft which is under the bone, as a hack or fist does.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and therefore this manner of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the sword pierces the bone above and senses it, and this manner of breaking is called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound from these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a stuck percussive blow, or a splitting or collar bone of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persisting break that approaches just to the tendon which is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is opened in the bone is as subtle as a mouse, and it is a small crack, and therefore this breaking is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound that is made or caused by striking with a stone, or falling, or something similar, and causes the bone fragment to go down, and it is hollow like when blacksmiths heat metal on furnaces.
si entre li piere dedens.	if into the bone inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those who have or whose head is moist like that of an infant;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and there occurs all these ways of breaking where small parts are dislodged as if they were.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak to him in his place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breakings by stripping away from them, and inquiring into tests, and through the corrupted flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it gently above, then opens up the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of gall, and loss of understanding, and extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes to come out and redden, and other similar things in more or less dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an unendurable accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounds come to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day if you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, otherwise the tendon below the bone will be corrupted, and the accidents we have said will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the break of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you split the split part thus:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and take the chief of the injured patient, and uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and on the shape of the wound as much as you can, and if blood flows from the dismemberment, or an abscess forms, provide the aid that is needed, and then fill the place with moist cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed down, and be assured of the cessation of blood flow.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One manner is that you bind at the constricting part before, and it's like this:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another cutting larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second manner is that you have many diverse constrictions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work lightly, so that you don't cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and strong, then it's necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer constrictions with tweezers, not too deep lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the testicle, and there should be above the point a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it's necessary for you to have many of them, so that each one comes to its place on the edge of the bone, so that you have tweezers for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of three types of parricides:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one parricide on the bone and turn to your two sides until you know the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then place the parricide elsewhere a little after, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertues, and make it more subtly than you can, and lightly, just as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is fitting that you take the apoplectin which remains of the bone to all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it must be more sharp and more subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it has none of the small bones or scales, then remove them lightly with the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound of tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is more sound;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the oath very strong, and it is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break appears more clearly; so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place below the head of this lenticular incisor, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut on one side only, and the wound should be in two parts, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chip away the bone all around, and take great care not to touch the membrane that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then remove it lightly, for one removes it without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not pierce all the way to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only on top, and there are small pieces, so it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to scrape away the scales with a fine scraper which you should have various quantities of, in order to make each place as suitable as possible, according to the work and figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then use coarse scrapers first, and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-like cuts and subtle breakings, it is necessary that you bring about a cause according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is not replied to by one who has put their study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the boil is uncovered, it's necessary that you take a cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do this as lightly as you can, so that you don't irritate the boil, then administer above the other layer, and don't strain it more than is necessary to keep the wound simply.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it be like this for one day or two, until the abscess is appeased, then loosen it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and vetch flour, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make powder of these things, and put it on the wound, and administer thereafter medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and wait until the wound is clean again, so you don't leave an ointment or let the bowels assemble above the brain's skin, for when the bowels gather above the brain's skin, they will run and burst forth, and the patient will suffer great harm.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you put a biting thing on the abscess, it necrotizes above it.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any evil accident befalls the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the swelling does not come forth except through the medicine you have put on, and it has such virtue, then it is necessary that you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix in one cloth, and apply it to the abscess.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then continue with the treatment by the means of treatments that are necessary, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nail above are broken, or one alone by itself, for they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and that part below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it becomes twisted or bent, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you plug your little nail or perforation of the nail with wax and put this breakage into your thumb's index finger, and then press firmly, until the nail regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and take care that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the neck, and it cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you put it equal at the head of a rod, rather large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do it the same way, and try to restore the first part as soon as you can, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	unless that, after seven or ten days, when the abscess is appeased, then plug at the top of the nail with linen cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you push one apart from the other, if there is a break within.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and be so large that they fill the hollows of the night.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said some physicians that one must soak tents in butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it should be moistened in the making of a poultice with egg whites and mill powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave the tent until the bone is hardened and the ligaments are toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one uses owl's down instead of tents, and if there is a soft wrapping around it, and the dislocation holds fast, and blows the patient through.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess appears on the neck while you are working there, then put cerate or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a small amount of aquilione.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess does not come forth, then apply an ointment by pouring out, with barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg whites, and place it on light fires, and do not bind the night.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	et if the breaking of the nail is small and it is broken into little pieces, so one would lead it to suitable instruments for this, then mend the breakage, and cure things in the same manner as plasters and ointments are suitable for this;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if there is no wound inside the nail, so one would treat it with tents, and put in plugs of pitch, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	(Note: This appears to be a title or heading, rather than a sentence to be translated)
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jawbone is out of place, and there is no wound to drain, and the break is only so slight that it is not actually broken in two, except perhaps inside, then one knows this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is on the right side, that you bite your two fingers and place them in the mouth of the patient.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the breakage is on the left side of the jaw, so bite your two fingers of the right hand, and gently insert the breakage into them, and set it straight with the other hand by degrees.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone break is separated into two pieces, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of teeth causes a gap or a routure, so strain them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then put a waxed pad on the broken jawbone and place a double cloth over it.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite,
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, then release it on the third day, and then set it back to its original shape.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and put plaster on top, with powder from the mill and a great deal of egg or fine wheat flour, after you have removed the gauze.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put a thin layer of plaster on top, and if the plaster dries, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes forth, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, leave no fragment of the bone that has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if the removal is done with subtle instruments fitting for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is none left, then sew the wound shut, if it is wide, and put on top suitable poultices to promote flesh, until they are healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forceful blow breaks many times before, towards the shoulder, and the breakage is in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where she is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is lighter to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is thus when there is no wound with the break, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken force.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other stretches out the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then place the break evenly between your knees, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor hindrance.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round wooden or woolen staff, and make it thick according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and stretch and lift the broken part, and strain the staff in your hand, so that you place the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcele forward because it comes out too far, then it is necessary that the patient lies comfortably on his hatrail, and put under the shoulder a middle-sized pillow, and have the assistants lower the shoulder so that the bone of the forcele is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the break to your knees, and if you find it fragmented, so it is necessary that you split it above.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and pull the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join for any adjustment, then cut at one of the dividers that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but make sure to put this instrument underneath the forceps, in order to hold the screw:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and shape like a spoon, and not be chipped, and be as wide as it is needed, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two handles, as you see, and one be large, and the other be strong, just like the shape of the wound that you made when you broke the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the breaking is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, then use the wound dressing and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes forth, then moisten one cloth with rose oil, and oil of lily, and wine, and put it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The treatment of bone, when it is without wounds and without trimming, is that you put powder from the mill and egg white on the bone, and light stoppers above, and place a spear below the saddle, if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide band of one palm's width, then put the cloth doubled above the stoppers and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin band of three fingers' width and length, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage are hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And put the band on the shoulder, and turn the bandage over the healthy side, and under the saddle sound, and under the saddle sick.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the shoulder well, and you clearly see that the band does not move on the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligaments relax, so restrain it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient sit on his back, and place him while he sleeps with a small pillow underneath the armpit, to lift the aid in high.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	so that the strain on the shoulder strap is eased by the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not unbind unless bad accidents come, up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the poultice, if you see that he needs it, and strain and leave it thus, until he is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and she is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and to some people in less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder break
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It often happens that the shoulder breaks or becomes loose, and it is not known to be inflamed except by the touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	so that you arrange it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then put powder of the mill on the joint with abundance of urine, and light bandages, and put it above the cloth doubled;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put a large and subtle needle above an cloth, a little bit larger than the shoulder, and under the needle are threads in some place of the shoulder, so bind those threads with linen bandages so that the needle stays even.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then bind it all with a great bandage firmly, so that the needle does not move from its place, and inspect the bond each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And every time it swells, bind it again, and put the needle back in its place if it is out of its place, and place the patient on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, then loosen it, and be careful, for it is not the bone that puts itself back together lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is bent forward and points downwards at the joint, then straighten it up and the bone, and do what we have said about calming down an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the rib.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The weight is sometimes broken in mid-air, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often enough.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in mid-air, then it falls downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and all, and by chance may vomit blood, and exposes the tendons in the broken bone, and one knows well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back, and he puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and carefully makes sure they are equal in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then puts on poultices and plasters above the plate of salt or another light fabric, and wraps it in a cloth, and ties it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turns the bandage around to the back, and holds it tightly, and rewards each hour with wine, and if it relapses, then he holds it tight.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to separate, because of corrosion or pruritus that comes to the site, or pain or abscess, then hasten and separate, and scrape off the swelling, and address what has come forth in ways of treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the swelling, and restrain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the breaking of the ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs does not occur except in very large men after the back, and at the top inside, and it does not bend except because they are flabby.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and he will feel it well during the examination that you must do.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you put equal pressure on the break, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind with an iron band, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of ribs is declining inward, then the patient feels very great pain and pricking, just as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and it leads to pricking, and all of them and vomiting great abundance of blood, and this is a grievous affliction, and the ancient ones have placed great cunning.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer meats that fill the belly, in order to push the break backward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this except when abscesses hot and present arise, if they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then it is healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that you put poultices on the joint to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, there is doubt whether the poultice attracts the superfluities to the joint due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us say that you should cover the joint with moist wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to set equal the breathing around, then take care of the treatment of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear through the bone which points to the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the joint of the broken ribcage, and it is necessary to put an instrument underneath to protect the flesh.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone and draw it lightly, and then sew shut the two lips of the wound if they are large, and treat with poultices until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if an abscess comes forth, then put damp cloths soaked in rose oil on it and apply them to the joint.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure while the place of it is suitable for an abscess, and be watchful on all sides where it should, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes a break occurs at the vertebra of the neck, and then it bends.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will be healed or not, then take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move nor stretch them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortally ill in many dispositions, and if he moves and feels well when they are strained and pressed, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient is being cured, if one applies care.
