Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, then take heed if the feet are soft, and if there are accidents in hand, and on the back sudden windiness and evacuation without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when one has cured it on his belly, then evacuation occurs without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is overcome on his back and wants to settle down, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not labor much in his healing.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, then the thing is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the remedy is that you apply oil of rose or oil of egg yolk on the spine if there is a hot abscess, so long as it is appeased;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then place one of the soothing and drying poultices on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover the wound with a splint;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a seam, and then treat it with ointment applying flesh until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", then put your pouch in your left hand and place it equal to your other hand at your power, then put the poultice and needle on, if you need them;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then pull it, and if there is a broken bone, do the same thing on it, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	When the hip bone is broken, and if it is, then there is a slight diminishment to the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and becomes longer, and declines at the pelvis, and comes to the patient with pain in the place, and punctures, and swells what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand above, as far as you are above the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and knows what kind of break it is and its shape is.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the break is only in the head, then set that break even, so that it be in natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it declines inwardly, so lie down the patient on their stomach until the restoration of that break is apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, then put on the plaster, and then put on a wooden or horn splint, and restrain the break, so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply the place below the ribs, until the ligaments are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their right side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if abscesses form there, do not touch them until the abscesses are appeased, and apply what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	and that's the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder break
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The adjutories are those things that are between the shoulder's top and its head, and if they are broken, one must restore them according to one of the two manners:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a fist-sized piece from the main growth, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And tie the two heads with two strings, and pull them up high, and make the patient sit on a siege;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then let it go with the broken arm on the fist, until it comes to the joint, and has about half a cubit of fist, then pull up on something heavy or have the minister extend it down.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the mirror's edge equal to his hands together, so that the edge returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you support the patient on their hat or headrest, and tie his hand to his neck; then instruct two attendants, one to hold what is above the break in his hands, and the other to hold below at each string, and stretch each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, so hold the ligament below the breastplate, and above the breastplate, and extend each of the assistants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the edge is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary that you place one end under the armpit, and the other at the back, under the edge.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the edge is at the back, then it is necessary to place one end slightly, without effort, so that the edge is equal above and below.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then set the edge equally as it should, and hold it, lest abscesses come to be there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses come to be there, do not hold it at all until seven days, and apply a warm poultice of linen and oil of roses, so that the abscesses are pacified.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then the restraint is, and the manner of restraining it is that you place the emplaster on the shoulder blade, then set the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put a cloth, and restrain it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its proper place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone is not broken, use stakes, and place a stake larger and stronger than the others on the shoulder blade, with two spaces between each stake, and have each stake be as long as it passes three palms on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then strain on the stakes, in the manner I said at the beginning of this chapter on the shoulder blade, stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the seating of the stars and the stretching, as we have said, in the cure that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, let it alone until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then look at each one after three days to see if the swelling or inflammation does not increase and come back to its place, or if the numbness cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you bind it, as we said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident comes, then do not release the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a layer of equal thickness of clean linen underneath the support, and look at each hour of the day or night to see if the shape of the broken member does not change, or if the bandage is loosening.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If he is addressed through the power of medicine, and gives him food that we have placed before him, in such a manner that the food be for the first subtle ones;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, if it is thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is custom that the assistant and the leg should be set back in forty days from then;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then one must loosen it and administer bath and ointment remedies to direct the joint.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and bound, so it must be untied in one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus", one of which is small and is that which supports the socket;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is large, and it is that which is below, towards the small toe;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance, one breaks only the great humerus, or the little one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the great ones are broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is a small bone that is broken alone, then it must be slightly extended and set even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a great bone, then it must be drawn out with greater force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and stretch it above the cushion, and hold the patient's hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others' bones, and let the patient cross over himself, with the cushion in front of him higher, that the patient does not suffer any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then stretch one of the ministers' arms to the part under his hand or to the joint, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any that are loose and cannot be held by force, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a splint and use an osteum, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if there is wound with bruising, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter;
si pren la cure.	Take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if abscesses appear in the beginning of the restoration, take a poultice made from rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and apply the poultice gently above, until the abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the poultice, and put an ointment made from flour powder mixed with a great deal of egg, then apply the candles, and let the candle on the edge be stronger and a little bit wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it should have six candles or arms in multiple positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	or whether the burn is on one of the bones or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and hold it more above the burn than elsewhere, and always less away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are on the dressing soft and moist, and not hard or dry.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and be the thread, from which it is strained, of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if some bad accident comes to the member, as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you wash the member with hot water, until those itchings are appeased.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not too tightly rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the stretching, and if the joint is relaxed and the bones are loosened, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little bit and leave it thus for some days until the swelling comes, and then bind.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or around it, then bind his hands to his neck, and let his necks be equal, and beware of movement and disturbance, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this dressing is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the bruise of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that behind the hand and in the fingers many bruises occur, and there is no other way than to bend them many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plantar aspect of the hand is broken or bent, it behooves the patient to cross his legs and sit straightly before him evenly.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then places his hand on the spread cloth and stretches out the broken bones, making them equal with the splints, until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies the poultice and bandages, unless an abscess comes, then he puts in a stake according to the quantity of the swelling.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth with a Y-fold.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is around the ankle joint of the foot, make a bundle of cloths and instruct the patient to wrap it tightly around his broken foot.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then strain it with a long cloth, and make the stake as thick as the plantar aspect of the hand, and strain it, as is fitting.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the bruise is on the outside, it is necessary that you put a bandage on top and another one underneath in the hand, so that the fingers be open and straight, then tie all around the hand, and stop the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of us from below, so it is a pouching, then set it even, as it should be;
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and strain with the sole, and if you see that putting a small straight stick will lift the fracture, and it does not move;
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is at other joints, such as in the index or one of the others, then set it even and bind it with a bandage that is behind;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together in one holding, as much as it is worth, or put on a splint like a pouched one;
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take heed in the restoration and setting of a hot abscess, and secure what comes out, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken shin
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and one sees it well when it turns in front and behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is such that one ties above the breakage, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face, then stretches each attendant to their equal share.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the tailbone, so that one of the ligaments points towards the fingernail, and the other ligaments are below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then let the straps be below the knee and the stretching be down.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the splints on the bone equal to his two hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the poultice, and the bandage, lest abscesses come there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, let it settle then return to your work and your treatment;
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is done in the same way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap above the breakage with bandages doubled in two or three places, and remove any superfluous parts, then turn the leg so that the toes come to the root of the knee, and tie a long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee on the underside, and let the end of the thread come up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn up on the leg and on the knee the bandage, then put on the breeching stays, and put one stay on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then employ the leather strap between the leg and the knee of soft cloth to put equal tension, then begin to bind strongly three or four turns on the breeching.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and when you go further up on the breeching, and loosen it less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two ends of the thread that you have placed between the leg and the knee, and tie three stays that are above, then return to the lower part at the head of the thread, until you come down below the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, until no swelling or abscess or other similar thing occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there is something wrong, then dislodge it, and address what comes next, just as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that are pricking, then it is necessary to remove them if one can;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if one cannot, then it is necessary to cut through the flesh and pull forth;
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until he is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And sometimes the cup of the shoulder is broken thus one puts in stones as in the apothecary and on the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	nevertheless, in the restoration done thus the patient does not get better.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the shin is restored in one day, or a little less or more, according to the diversities of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the swelling of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Knows that in the bend of the knee there is slight breaking, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it's not more than a crack or a pore, and it occurs in every wound, and without a wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when one puts back what is bent to its joints, as long as it can be moved.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then put the poultice on, and place a rounded stone if you need to, and bind it as is necessary, then reward all the preparations that we have said for other breakages, such as an abscess and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he sets to each accident what is due to him, so long as he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Know that in the leg there are two bones, for which one is called by its right name "tibia", and the other is called "fibula";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it happens with all sorts of breakage as it comes to the arm, and for that reason is the restoration such as that of the arm equally, and the works are all done. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns wrong in every way.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well;
et torne desoz.	and turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then apply an extension, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but always, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be smaller and more gentle;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and bind according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed all your work, take two straps of ash-colored wood that encircle the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the kneecap down.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two layers of cloth above and below, and bind it securely in the middle as well, so that at this point the leg cannot bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should minister to the bones of the long length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and set the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this in the break or where there is injury.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cures as long as he is sound.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot do break and two or three pieces, and in most cases it does not exceed more than four dispositions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has a break in the bone of his foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground, where the bones are lifted up, and press it until they return to their place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the poultice and bandages on top, and under the foot of the foot a small piece of cloth to two full shoes, then strain the foot gradually, after you have wrapped around cloths and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if he has any of his toes broken, restore them, as we have said about the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put an splint on the broken toe according to its length, and make it slightly larger, then put that piece of cloth I mentioned under the foot, and strain it gradually.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, break them; and place a stake on each one according to its size, wrapped in one fold of linen, and tie the table beneath the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be so that on top of the stake is the opening of the table to go into the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you not forget the other things I have said about other breakages, since we have spoken;
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it deserves.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bones of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of natural womanhood is broken, make her sit with an enlarged pelvis, then incline her towards the back part, and let it be held by the rear.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the natural opening of the patient with cotton, and put in as much as the stomach is.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then push away the woman, and lift the small of the back piece by piece, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and return the bone with its stop.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, then remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back on, and do this for seven days or around.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	and then the break will be restored, and if you see, take a sheep's bladder, and tie it to the penis with a cord, and pour all the bladder into nature.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cord strongly, until the bladder is emptied inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the nature will return to the break.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be filled with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the finger of man or woman is broken, restore it thus as we have said in the bone of the hare.
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these breaks are not hidden from him who puts his study and use there and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the break signifies the right path of restoration in many dispositions.
enten le donques.	then understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the splint, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert it into the splint;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it with cloth, and leave it for three days or eight around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a break with an open wound, whether it be large like the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, to heal now, as the wounds that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing, but then becomes infected with vinegar, and you have nothing else, then begin to restore the breakage in that same hour or day, lest abscesses form and do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses form, then leave the restoration alone for nine days, until the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, lest you bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the surface of the skin, it is necessary that you place it in slight extension with your hands.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension is not ready to put equal with your hands, then reattach it with this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and therefore it is necessary for the doctor to take three or four of them, according to what he needs in each treatment of a break.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be round and somewhat big, that it does not bend at all to the compression on the member in your work, and be arched forward, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it is necessary that the curved bone be placed on top of the apparent head of the bone;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and tie it once, until it recovers, and let it be even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the top of the bone, until the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we said, then use a suitable instrument to this end, or chisel or gouge, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then gather up what remains in the bone of roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	So do this until it is in its place, then soak the cloth in black medicinal wine, and properly clean what remains.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put any cerate or other substance on the wound where there is oil, unless you make it bring purification and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer ointments when you have restored the bone, and let the wound be uncovered, and cover the surrounding area entirely, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the breakage.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, and they have brought upon the patient or death or corruption sometimes;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and be the stitches more soft and gentler than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil consequences may come from it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put ointments on.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but wrap around, instead of ointments, hard cloths and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the bow to the wound, so take away what you put on top with all wine, and put in healing ointment for wounds, just as four-leafed ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you stretch the member two times a day, morning and evening, until it is fixed and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are aligned in such a way that the bow string runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it happens that way for several days, and it cannot heal but instead swells again, know that there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you cover the wound with a tent, and remove all these disjointed pieces that bring forth that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, so it is necessary that you cure it, according to what is written in its chapter before this.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and appears on top of the member, just like the bones of the hip or shoulder, and other similar ones from the large members, do not pull it, for many times death ensues, but let it stay until it can be fixed.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	by chance it will fall out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can;
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of boils that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often see after the breaking of bones, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a sad thing to behold the figure of the member.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance the member cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take care then if our nail is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if the administrator administers stiptic medicines, such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acaica, and similar others, then take one of these things or all together, and mix it with wine, stiptic vinegar, or with an abundance of egg whites, or with oil.
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and places it on the nightstand in bed, and holds it tight, and does not remove it for three days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then unbinds it, and starts another one, until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or you bind on a well-made linen bandage;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of the linen is that it removes all swellings from above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the swelling has already become hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut on top, and make the excess apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you put it in someone's hands until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the break in the bone is restored, and remains after the weak and subtle limbs, since it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many ties, and could not come the nourishment to the member;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of abundance of swelling;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or because of too great movements, not at its own time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make their body soft, until the blood is multiplied in them;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer bath, and give it joy and ease;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then put pitch on the member, so that the pitch attracts to the great swelling, and draws out often with water till the swelling goes into the member;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the twisted member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken apart, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	so do not believe the foolish people who say that one should break the member all over again, and many foolish physicians have done so in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and brings great evils, and by chance death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the swellings and tortures are fresh, then it is necessary that they be applied with hot water, or herbs that soften, such as plantain leaves, roots, and mullein, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the plaster should be made soothing, such as diachylon well made, and you take the poultice of plantain, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	You take greasy figs, and crush them with henbane, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And at any time remove the swelling by continuous and lengthy rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And there should be a gentle movement to each limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling is hardened and calcified, like stone, and it needs to be opened with iron, so you must cut just up to the bone, with a fine, subtle incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and put sense and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, so it is necessary now to bring it back into place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if one delays, the swelling will increase, and by chance, if one puts pressure on the swelling.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	therefore it is not fitting to move him until he has deflated.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times brings on spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this happens, if it makes the patient better, then leave him, until the abscess is pacified.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then wet the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the treatment comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	The jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	or they are slightly pulled out of their places, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the breast, and the saliva from the mouth cannot be held, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps around its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through many gentle procedures.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly, and not hesitate at all;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient, and puts the mirror's speculum into one of his hands in the root of the jawbone dislocation within the mouth, if the dislocation is into two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands be free to make it even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften his jawbone, and move it from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers put it back in place, until it returns to its natural position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is stiffened, even if both jawbones together are stuck, so raise them with hot water and oil, until they become slightly loose.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not neglect the setting back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are set back evenly, and the patient's mouth feels well-mollified, so put on moist cloths in a poultice made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with moist bandages.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient sleeps on his back, and his legs being between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor does he strain himself at all, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jawbones are freed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then let him eat as he likes lightly, and do not trouble to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jawbone is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their natural state, then fevers and sore habits ensue, and possibly also bowel looseness, and possibly also vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a misfortune;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times the person who has it will die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot dislocate from the chest within its continuity and from the breastbone, and is dislocated sometimes to the back, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies comfortably on his back, and stretches out his arms.
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint strongly onto your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the poultice and the bandage, and tighten it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the shoulder that is near the cut cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it does dislocate once, then reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the poultice and bandage, and bind it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus also bring back the head of the shoulder when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one of which is when it dislocates at the base of the neck below.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part of the breast;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance it dislocates above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and many times it dislocates downward toward the neck, especially in those who have little flesh, for they jump forth hastily;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Those who have enough fat, jump away from stones, and return to stones.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they receive a blow or bruise, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and thinks it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary then that you try it out, until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation occurs when it falls downward towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find a pit at the top of the shoulder, and under the shoulder blade touching the top of the shoulder, just as if it were an ox.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand back to their neck, nor move at all with any movements.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the touching point.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this kind of dislocation is not for anything but to bring back when it is new or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the servant lifts the patient's hand high up, then places the straps underneath the armpit, and lifts the joint upwards with force to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the servant lifts the hand and stretches it high up, then places it underneath.
si venra hastanment.	so it will come to be quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it doesn't come as we said in three days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the amnestor should moisten and soothe it, as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and bring it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then cover the patient with a blanket on their back, and put underneath the armpit a layer of wool equal, not too soft nor too hard, then place the fingers of the patient's hand; lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other attendants hold the patient's head so he does not move down;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder comes back to its place now, and if you see that you are repositioning it in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and that you make someone larger than the patient be present;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and it should be straight towards the patient's side, and push the shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift up the armpit so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant pulls the patient's hand down towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can hold with him something heavy, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And reposition it in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and that's when you put a long poker in the ground, whose head is as steady as a piston, and not too big or too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be put under the patient, but so that it has wrapped itself softly above, and the patient is leaning on the long piece of wood;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then her hand will be extended below on the other side forming, and the jointure will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, so do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a piece of iron, two hands long and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded so that it may enter deeply under the shoulder blade, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then tie it above the head of the fist wrapped so that the fist does not hurt the patient, then place it under the shoulder blade of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend your arm above the fist of length, and tie the aid above the fist, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on top of one shoulder blade of width, and let the hands go down below, and leave the body hanging from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint comes together now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is returned, in whatever way that may be, then it is necessary that you put below the socket a ball of wool evenly, then apply the poultice around with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, on all the shoulder and around, then strain below the socket gently, and turn the cloth on the poultice, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he be patient a little while until the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then be patient again after three days or seven, and move him;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if he is stiff and has not been softened, it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cauterization at three places, as is written before this chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this and he slips after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm above, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is torn or stretched or loosened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the chest, or shoulders, or back, is caused by impulse and stretching of hands, and another instrument is administered.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal so long as he is sound.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes swelling in the member and delayed movement, then the patient should take many baths until that swelling is alleviated and the member returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated to points, and to points it returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it has dislocated in all parts, and even before and behind, and the dislocation is not set right, for one can see it well and feel it well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's shoulder with the skin, so you can see it plainly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it as soon as the swelling comes to life, for if the swelling came to life, it would be hard to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be completely set right, even when it is at the back;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	so it is worse than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and by chance many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is such that when it can be reset, you stretch his hand with your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms be spread out, and the hands of the mirror according to the cut around, above, and below, and bind the joint to his buttocks together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes it to the root of the palm onto the shoulder that is out of place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong stretching;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm and hold it firmly, so that it does not move with the stretching;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm on each side, then having wrapped a double fold long and wide around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the nurse has bound the joint to her hand, she anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then binds the joint firmly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, then applies dry powder with some egg white, and binds it firmly, and bends the arm to the patient's neck, and leaves it for some days, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is firm in its place, then release the ligament and let it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	And if you see that the joint does not bind well, then reapply the poultice and the ligament, and let it be thus for some days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	Then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels stiffness after the realignment of the joint, and it becomes swollen, then bathe it well and massage it gently, and press until it is relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	Or you put a layer of fat sheep's wool on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter into water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when he sweats, then massage the joint temperately, then put the wool back on, and then enter into water.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus two or three times, until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, put a cloth soaked in warm cow's milk with butter on top;
si revenra a sa disposition.	so it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joints of the hand are dislocated, and the swelling is light, more so than in other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place quickly, in the same way that it is dislocated, as long as the swelling is hot or an abscess comes forth.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the remedy is that you put the ailing hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of your hand, and place the palm of your hand so that it meets the appearance of the jointure, and press down until it recovers.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is necessary for you to check if it is well in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the patient's hand on a table at the extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts their back on their hand on the table, and the doctor puts their hand on that appearance of the jointure.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If she returns now, it's well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	Unless, if the strain of soothing ointments calms abscesses thus, and it is left in this way without recommencing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and nothing harms the patient except until the hand is softened, and cannot strain anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then you know that the nerves are cut or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy except to strain through burning by case, and it may not be worth anything by chance.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then strain and leave it for five days, then displace and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is some swelling, apply warm water to it, and rub it until it is sound.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Sometimes the tendons of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or stomach;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then the tendon is set and push the dislocation into your pockets as much as it retracts, then support the head of the tendon and draw it towards the part where it is detached;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, then set it even on that day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and tie the nut with what we said, and loosen the joint of a day, and make it move, and re-tie the nut;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often until it is straight, and also do so if it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, and do it just as you did before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and also do this when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	and treatment of the hump on the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hump on the back or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no treatment, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the evacuations occur without one's will, nor can they be held, and many times a certain member, or both breasts, or two arms, or one is softened.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the shin bone moves into four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	the one that moves in back is called "gilbositez";
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the cure is that you reward if the goutiness has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there isn't any cure or healing at all.
