Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falls or blows or similar things, the old ways of curing say great things through big words, but there is little profit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the goutiness that comes before the stomach, there is no remedy nor health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which comes straightly in both sides, and one cannot cure fevers except for that which comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient be stretched on his face in one equal place and have some strain under him, so he does not get hurt;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then drive the iron spike into the ground firmly, and another to the feet, and bind a cord between the straps of the patient, and another to the thighs, and knees, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two assistants know the bonds, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two iron spikes.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the spike as we have said, and the physicians put their palms on the spine firmly, until it relents.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not relent with this treatment, take a board three arm-lengths long, and hollow out the bottom of it, and the patient lies on his side, and push the top of the board under the back, then place the middle of the board on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and the physicians put their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it relents to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, make him do it to the one who turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	and you make two blisters on the head of the patient's great arm, and towards the feet two others, with a hand's breadth between each blister, one above the other.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each blister one pore, where the worm runs through, and let the blisters be firmly fixed to the ground, so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each two blisters be one blister turning, on which the worms turn, and have in the two turnings two small blisters a hand's breadth long, to turn the worm;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is between the knots to the worm going towards the head, and the other cord to the other knot at the foot, and each of the servants turns his worm along the entire cord, and the master makes it even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Et quant elle est igalz, so put on desiccating plaster with abundance of egg white, and then bind, and then apply an ointment from a tablet of three inches long that procures the place of gibbosity and the part of the spine to be whole, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use gentle massage on the patient, until he is well.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if nothing comes to the end of the health, it is necessary to administer soothing and easing medications, with the ointment that we have said above.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes one administers a piece of linseed, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back part of the spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and that is the bone which opens, why one should not have presumption about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	by chance would death come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder do not come forth except with dislocations alone, nor does it come so with other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	within and without, and before and behind;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and further within than that, and pulled dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when one joins the diseased leg to the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee sticks out more than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot double their knee in fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the leg that is under swollen apostemal heat, because the head of the groin comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens on the outside is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	The signs of one who has this condition before him are that he is well proportioned in his leg according to completion.
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	Everywhere, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells with anger, and when he goes, it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens in back is that he cannot spread his kneecap, nor double it, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and the anger is softened, and is the head of the hip at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are that you should treat if the dislocation is ancient and it remains according to its condition, and there is no care.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not necessary that he have presumptuousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in that one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, then hasten to return the joint, and stretch inside and outside, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	by chance if it will return, and there is no need for another care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you appear the minister strong, and strengthen the leg by two hands, or by one ligament that is tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister stretches his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands under his armpits, then tightens a soft ligament above the hip.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another pulls the end of the ligament.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch it up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at one time, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to three similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, just as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If not, then it is necessary to make an incision according to its likeness.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the hip-joint, then it is necessary that you place the patient on his healthy side, then put the ligament above the root of the hip, and the end which is below the angle, then stretch the ligament upwards towards the angle, and towards the femur.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	Then take another assistants' arms, and embrace the thick part of the ailing person's hip, and stretch it forward firmly:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	so it will return to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot bind it in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two legs of the patient together with a soft strap on the two heels and on the two knees, and let the sick leg be stretched two doits more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it should be suspended from the top of a beam, and be above the ground two arms long;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct the assistant to embrace the head of the hip, and have another assistant holding with the patient, who should hold firmly the hip, because the joints are returning quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in the back, then lie down the patient, just as we have said in the case of gilboesitey, and stretch out the cloth above the afflicted leg properly, and also above the pelvis.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two spits, one at the head and the other at the hips, then insert the spit between the patient's thighs in the shape.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have damp cloths wrapped around, so that the patient does not bleed, then stretch each attendant towards him, and place the mirror next to his hand on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put it on the table, and press it thus as we have said in gilbositeit, and lay the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, then it is necessary to extend the afflicted leg quickly, and according to what I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the mirror so that it is on top of the afflicted knee, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the kneecap.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, it does not need to stretch out the patient downwards or lift them up towards the earth, but rather should be as if the hip were dislocated at the back, as we have said about lying on two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on their face, and the strap should be stretched as we have said before, and must not press on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be in place when the patient stretches out their legs, and they will be equal.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and apply the poultice, and strain it with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and if he rests for three days or four, then loosen it, and apply the poultice on top;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are equal, then strain it again, as before, and leave it for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then loosen it, and let it go gently, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The joints are dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, inwardly and outwardly, and backward.
et ne desalue point devant.	and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg to their hip, and if it does not bend at the hip, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all of them is that you make the patient sit up straight, and stretch their leg if they can, and put your back against their face, and place their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take their kneecap between your palms, and draw it inwards between your two arms, then bend the two sides of the kneecap sharply.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister stretches their foot until the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it bends slightly at the hip.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put on the poultice, and make the leg rest at the hip, and tie it together tightly for three days or four, then loosen it;
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not bother the patient to walk until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, strong extension should be administered, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tend before the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return is lighter, and one should stretch it lightly with his hands when he is only slightly stretched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated entirely, then you should make the patient sit upright, and hold him tight with one minister only by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then draw the foot to you at your right hand, and then to your left two times, then stretch it upwards, and pull the foot well up;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it's well;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	but if not, then start the work again, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it can't return like that, make the patient sit on the ground with their back to the earth, and place one leg firmly on the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around so the patient doesn't hurt;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then take hold of the leg, and another attendant should stretch out the foot to their hands or to the binding strap that ties around the ankle;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then each attendant should stretch equally, and the straps should be there between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when one is stretching;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then put the fingers equally on the dislocation at their hands, and another attendant should take hold of the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is fixed in place, then put the poultice and bandages on top, and bind firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle at the back, so that the ligament is not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then let it be for two or three days, and if the ligament swells, then bind.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then release it on the fourth day, and prohibit the patient from walking for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess bursts forth, it is necessary to lance it, as we have said elsewhere, until he is healed.
des dois	you must
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are dislocated, you should gently stretch them without effort, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or heel of the foot, then it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a plain floor or on a level table exactly straight, and place your foot on what appears to be this joint, then press firmly with your foot until it is restored.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is equal and there is nothing appearing, so put a two-legged table under the sole of the foot, then strain them strongly, and leave it for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation and one seeks to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not modest in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and tardy, nor too bold;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and start with gentle soothing things on the hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the member to its place, so that the abscess may come to life;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is at rest, administer soothing things to abscesses hot, and treat the wound as it should be, with ointments dried.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a breakage with dislocation, and small bones separated, set them and do what we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering the path of fear, as I have said, for this brings harm according to your Creator, and for the strength of your arm and body.
